### Frontend Livewire

- [x] **M22 — N+1 (NxM) queries when recalculating extras/options pricing for cart selections**
  - **Fixed:** Both `recalculateExtrasPricing()` and `recalculateOptionsPricing()` now batch-load their models once with `findMany(...)->keyBy('id')` (1 query instead of E×S `find()` calls), then index inside the loops. For extras I `clone` the batch-loaded model per `priceForDates()` call because `Extra::priceForDates()` mutates `$this->price` (dynamic pricing) — reusing one instance would compound the adjustment across selections. Independent review found `OptionValue::priceForDates()` is non-mutating (returns `$this->price->multiply(...)`, never assigns), so the options path reuses the instance without cloning. The per-selection dynamic-pricing sub-query is inherent and out of scope. Added `test_extras_dynamic_pricing_is_applied_per_selection_not_compounded` (verified it fails with the compounded `6.60` if the clone is removed); the existing aggregation tests regression-cover the refactor.
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/AvailabilityMultiResults.php:360-400`
  - **Problem:** recalculateExtrasPricing() re-fetches Extra::find($extra['id']) inside the inner foreach over $selectionDataArrays (line 372), once per (extra x selection) pair, and each priceForDates() call additionally runs a dynamic-pricing query (Extra::priceForDates -> getDynamicPricing). recalculateOptionsPricing() has the identical pattern with OptionValue::find($option['value']) (line 393). For E extras and S selections this is ExS model loads plus their pricing sub-queries on every addSelections/removeSelection/updateExtras round-trip. Confirmed.
  - **Fix:** Batch-load the models once before the outer map: `$extras = Extra::findMany($ids)->keyBy('id');` then index inside the loops. Do NOT naively hoist a single Extra::find() out of only the inner loop and reuse the same instance across selections: priceForDates() mutates $this->price (Extra.php:113 `$this->price = $dynamicPricing->applyRest(...)`), so a reused instance would compound the dynamic-pricing mutation across iterations. Either clone per priceForDates call, batch-load fresh instances, or refactor priceForDates to be non-mutating (then batch-load and reuse safely).
  - **Evidence:** Lines 368-378: `->map(function ($extra) use ($selectionDataArrays) { ... foreach ($selectionDataArrays as $selectionData) { $totalPrice->add(Price::create(Extra::find($extra['id'])->priceForDates($selectionData))); } ...`. Lines 389-399 mirror with OptionValue::find. Extra::priceForDates (Extra.php:106-122) calls getDynamicPricing (a query) and mutates $this->price at line 113.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-performance sweep(s)_

- [x] **M23 — resetOnBoot resets search data and re-dispatches on EVERY request, not just initial load**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/AvailabilitySearch.php:58-65`
  - **Problem:** boot() in Livewire 3/4 runs on every component request (initial mount AND every subsequent update/action), not only first load. With resetOnBoot=true the block at lines 60-64 unconditionally sets data->quantity=1, data->rate=null and calls search(true) on every request, which dispatches 'availability-search-updated' with the reset payload each time. When live=true, updatedData() can then dispatch a second search() in the same request. So enabling resetOnBoot would make rate/quantity selection unstable. Correctly identified as a design bug for the resetOnBoot=true path. Severity recalibrated to medium (not high): resetOnBoot defaults to false (line 38), there are no tests/usages enabling it in-repo, and the property is #[Locked] so only the consuming Blade can opt in.
  - **Fix:** Move the reset/initial-search logic from boot() into mount(), which runs once per component lifecycle: `public function mount(): void { if ($this->resetOnBoot) { $this->data->quantity = 1; $this->data->rate = null; $this->search(true); } }`. If first-load-only semantics must stay outside mount, gate the block with a non-persisted guard flag so it does not re-run on hydrated requests.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 58-65: `public function boot(): void { if ($this->resetOnBoot) { $this->data->quantity = 1; $this->data->rate = null; $this->search(true); } }`. search() (95-110) always `$this->dispatch('availability-search-updated', $this->data)`. updatedData() (88-93) calls search() again when live. Livewire boot() runs on every request. resetOnBoot defaults false (line 38) and has no in-repo consumer.
  - _Livewire · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M24 — handleFirstStep advances to step 2 even when assignExtras/assignOptions fail**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Checkout.php:207-211`
  - **Problem:** assignExtras() and assignOptions() (Checkout.php:558-582) catch sync exceptions, call $this->addError(...) and `return` — but that return only exits the helper, not handleFirstStep(). handleFirstStep then unconditionally runs `$this->step = 2;` (line 211). The reservation's total/payment are written at line 205 BEFORE the sync (lines 208-209), so a sync failure leaves the price persisted but the extras/options pivot rows not attached, and the user advances to the personal-details step. They can subsequently pay an amount that no longer matches what is actually attached. Likelihood is low (requires a DB error/deadlock on sync) but the consequence is a charge/inventory mismatch, so medium severity is appropriate.
  - **Fix:** Make assignExtras()/assignOptions() return a success boolean (or rethrow) and gate the advance: `if (! $this->assignExtras() || ! $this->assignOptions()) { return; }` before `$this->step = 2;`.
  - **Evidence:** Checkout.php:558-569 assignExtras catches Exception, addError, `return` (helper-local). Lines 207-211: `$this->assignExtras(); $this->assignOptions(); $this->step = 2;` with no success check. Total/payment written at line 205 before the sync.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M25 — ReservationCreated side effects are not transactional with reservation creation — a thrown AvailabilityException leaves an orphan PENDING reservation**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesReservationQueries.php:77-98`
  - **Problem:** createReservation() persists the PENDING Reservation row (lines 77-92) and is NOT wrapped in a transaction, then dispatches ReservationCreated whose synchronous listeners run in $listen order: AddAffiliateToReservation, AddDynamicPricingsToReservation, DecreaseAvailability, AddReservationIdToSession (ResrvProvider.php:111-114). DecreaseAvailability -> AvailabilityRepository::decrement() throws AvailabilityException when stock ran out (AvailabilityRepository.php:171-173). The caller checkout() catches AvailabilityException (AvailabilityResults.php:174) and shows an error, but the PENDING row already exists, no stock was decremented, and AddReservationIdToSession (which runs AFTER DecreaseAvailability) never executes — so resrv_reservation is never set in the session. That orphan PENDING row is therefore NOT reachable by the session-based cleanup in ExpireReservations (lines 27-29) and only gets swept by the time-based loop IF minutes_to_hold is configured (it is optional). For the cart path createMultiReservation(), parent+children commit in a DB::transaction (lines 126-153) but ReservationCreated is dispatched AFTER commit (line 155), so a throw on child N>1 leaves children 1..N-1 already decremented and the parent+children rows committed — partial, inconsistent stock state. validateAvailabilityAndPrice() runs first and narrows the race window, but the TOCTOU gap between that check and the locked decrement is real.
  - **Fix:** Wrap createReservation() in a DB::transaction and either dispatch ReservationCreated inside it (so a DecreaseAvailability throw rolls back the reservation row) or, if events must fire post-commit, have a DecreaseAvailability failure delete/expire the just-created reservation. For createMultiReservation, perform the child decrements inside the same creation transaction (or roll back the parent on any child failure) so stock can't be left partially decremented. At minimum, set the session id before decrementing so an orphan is session-cleanable.
  - **Evidence:** createReservation: `$reservation = Reservation::create([... 'status' => PENDING ...]); ReservationCreated::dispatch(...)` with no surrounding transaction. $listen order puts DecreaseAvailability (113) before AddReservationIdToSession (114). decrement throws: `throw new AvailabilityException(__('Not enough availability for this rate.'));`. checkout() catches only AvailabilityException. createMultiReservation dispatches ReservationCreated at line 155, AFTER the DB::transaction closes at 153.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-concurrency, livewire-availability sweep(s)_

### Vue / CP UI

- [x] **M26 — ExtraConditionsForm aliases and mutates the parent extra's nested conditions array (prop mutation)**
  - **Where:** `resources/js/components/ExtraConditionsForm.vue:134-141`
  - **Problem:** onMounted assigns conditionsForm.value = props.data directly (line 136), where props.data is ExtraConditionsPanel.conditionsSafe() returning props.data.conditions.conditions (ExtraConditionsPanel.vue:78). That nested array is the live object handed down via Extras.vue editConditions(item) -> extra.value = item (Extras.vue:182-185), which itself is an element of category.extras coming from ExtrasList's categories ref. Since conditionsForm is the SAME reference, every add() push (line 144), remove() splice (line 157), clearValues() and v-model edit mutates the parent extra.conditions.conditions in place before the user saves. Cancelling the panel does not revert the in-memory change. In practice the damage is masked because saving triggers extraConditionsSaved() -> getAllExtras() -> reload-categories (full server reload), but cancelling without saving leaves the mutated array, and other UI bound to that extra (e.g. extraHasConditions badge at Extras.vue:209-211) can reflect unsaved edits. The prop-mutation anti-pattern is real.
  - **Fix:** Deep-clone on ingest in onMounted: conditionsForm.value = Array.isArray(props.data) ? props.data.map(c => ({ ...c })) : []; (or structuredClone). Never assign a prop-derived reference to a ref you then mutate via push/splice/v-model.
  - **Evidence:** Line 136: `conditionsForm.value = Array.isArray(props.data) ? props.data : [];` assigns the same array. ExtraConditionsPanel.vue:78 `return props.data.conditions.conditions || [];` returns the live nested array. Extras.vue:182-184 `function editConditions(item) { extra.value = item;` passes the live object. add()/remove()/clearValues() all mutate conditionsForm.value directly.
  - _Vue · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: vue-fieldtypes-composables sweep(s)_

- [x] **M27 — v-for over conditions uses array index as :key, breaking row identity on insert/remove**
  - **Where:** `resources/js/components/ExtraConditionsForm.vue:6`
  - **Problem:** Line 6 uses v-for="(condition, index) in conditionsForm" :key="index". remove(index) splices a middle row (line 157), shifting all subsequent indices, so Vue reuses DOM/component instances for different logical conditions. The rows contain stateful child fieldtypes (time-fieldtype with v-model:value at lines 31/34, DateRangePicker at 23, Selects, Input) whose internal/uncontrolled state and focus can stick to the wrong logical row after a mid-list removal. Validation error mapping (errors['conditions.' + index + ...]) is recomputed from the new index so it re-binds correctly to the new positions, but the child-component-state mismatch is the classic index-key bug and is real. Medium severity is reasonable given the stateful children, though the practical impact is limited (conditions lists are short and removal is occasional).
  - **Fix:** Assign a stable client key when a condition is created/hydrated (e.g. _key: crypto.randomUUID() in add() and when ingesting props.data) and use :key="condition._key". Strip the synthetic key in handleDates before emitting/saving.
  - **Evidence:** Line 6 `<div v-for="(condition, index) in conditionsForm" :key="index" ...>`; remove() at line 156-158 `conditionsForm.value.splice(index, 1);`. Children use v-model on conditionsForm[index].* (e.g. line 31 `<time-fieldtype v-model:value="conditionsForm[index].time_start" />`).
  - _Vue · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M28 — Cutoff fieldtype marks the entry dirty on every page load**
  - **Where:** `resources/js/fieldtypes/Cutoff.vue:99-104,146-148`
  - **Problem:** On mount, when the entry already exists (!newItem) Cutoff.vue unconditionally calls updateFieldValue() (line 102). updateFieldValue() emits a freshly-allocated object: update(enabled.value ? { ...settings, schedules: [...settings.schedules] } : null) (line 147). Statamic's Publish Field.vue short-circuits identical updates via strict equality (valueUpdated: `if (value === existingValue) return;`), then Container.vue deep-watches values and calls dirty() on any change. A brand-new object reference is never === the stored object, so for any entry whose Cutoff field holds a settings object (cutoff enabled), opening the entry immediately flags it as having unsaved changes even when the user touched nothing. (When cutoff is disabled it emits null, and if the stored value was already null the === short-circuit prevents the dirty, so the false-dirty is specific to enabled-cutoff entries.) Other resrv fieldtypes avoid this because they emit a stable primitive string that the === check absorbs.
  - **Fix:** Do not push a new object on mount. Remove the `if (!newItem.value) { updateFieldValue(); }` call from onMounted (line 101-103); the deep watch on settings (line 106) and the toggle/add/remove handlers already emit on genuine edits. If an initial sync is truly needed, compare against props.value and only emit when the locally-built object actually differs (e.g. deep-equal check), or emit the exact same reference held in props.value.
  - **Evidence:** Cutoff.vue line 102 `updateFieldValue();` inside onMounted; line 147 `update(enabled.value ? { ...settings, schedules: [...settings.schedules] } : null);` (new object literal each call). vendor Publish/Field.vue:96-100 `function valueUpdated(value) { const existingValue = data_get(...); if (value === existingValue) return; setFieldValue(...); }` — object refs are never ===, so setFieldValue runs. vendor Publish/Container.vue:161-168 `watch(values, (values) => { dirty(); ... }, { deep: true })` and dirty() adds to Statamic.$dirty. Contrast Availability.vue:161 `update(enabled.value)` which emits a string and is absorbed by the === check.
  - _Vue · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M29 — Refund action exposed in the listing UI with no permission gating (route also unprotected)** _(resolved by H9: refund route now behind `can:use resrv`; covered by CpRoutePermissionTest. Client `v-if` gate is a no-op since the listing page itself requires `use resrv`.)_
  - **Where:** `resources/js/pages/Reservations/Index.vue:114-117`
  - **Problem:** The prepended-row-actions slot always renders a 'Refund' DropdownItem (Index.vue:116) which PATCHes props.refundUrl (refund(), lines 51-64). The backing route resrv.reservation.refund (routes/cp.php:57) carries no can: middleware, unlike the export routes which are explicitly wrapped in Route::middleware('can:use resrv') (cp.php:73-77). Because the addon registers these under the $routes['cp'] group, they sit behind CP authentication but NOT behind any resrv permission, so any authenticated CP user who can reach the page can issue a real refund + state transition (ReservationCpController::refund, lines 195-234, which performs gateway->refund() then transitionTo(REFUNDED)). The 'use resrv' permission exists (ResrvProvider::bootPermissions, ~line 322) and is applied to nav items but not to this route. Existing tests (ReservationCpTest) only run as the default super-admin and never assert permission gating, so the gap is untested. The primary fix is server-side; the Vue client gate is secondary.
  - **Fix:** Add authorization to the route/controller: wrap the refund route in ->middleware('can:use resrv') (or a dedicated 'refund reservations' permission) so it cannot be bypassed. Then pass a canRefund boolean from indexCp() (based on $user->can(...)) and wrap the Refund DropdownItem in v-if="canRefund" for UX. Client gating alone is insufficient.
  - **Evidence:** routes/cp.php:57 `Route::patch('/resrv/reservation/refund', 'ReservationCpController@refund')->name('reservation.refund');` - no ->can(). Contrast cp.php:73 `Route::middleware('can:use resrv')->group(...)` around exports. Index.vue:116 unconditionally renders the Refund item.
  - _security · confirmed · high confidence_

### Affiliate / Customer / Data / Misc

- [x] **M30 — Abandoned-email dedupe by email but marking by customer_id causes repeat sends**
  - **Where:** `src/Console/Commands/SendAbandonedReservationEmails.php:38-63`
  - **Problem:** The command dedupes recipients by email (`->unique(fn ($reservation) => $reservation->customer->email)`, line 40) but stamps `abandoned_email_sent_at` only on rows sharing the kept reservation's `customer_id` (`->where('customer_id', $reservation->customer_id)`, lines 59-61). Customers are created fresh per checkout with no email dedup (CheckoutForm.php:106 `Customer::create`, HandlesReservationQueries.php:167 `Customer::create`), so one person who abandons two reservations gets two distinct customer_id rows. After the first run only the kept reservation's customer_id is stamped; the other reservation(s) with the same email keep `abandoned_email_sent_at = NULL`, are re-selected by the `whereNull` filter on the next cron run, and trigger another email to the same address. This repeats once per extra customer_id until those rows age out or get stamped. The precondition (same person abandoning multiple checkouts) is realistic (retry-then-abandon). Existing tests (ReservationAbandonedTest) only exercise the single-shared-customer_id case, so this gap is uncovered.
  - **Fix:** Stamp by the recipient email rather than customer_id so every reservation sharing that email is marked in one pass, e.g. `$reservations->filter(fn ($r) => $r->customer->email === $reservation->customer->email)->each(fn ($r) => $r->update(['abandoned_email_sent_at' => now()]));`. This realigns the dedupe key with the marking key.
  - **Evidence:** Line 40 dedupes by `$reservation->customer->email`; lines 59-61 stamp by `->where('customer_id', $reservation->customer_id)`. CheckoutForm.php:106 and HandlesReservationQueries.php:167 both call `Customer::create([...])` with no lookup-by-email, so the same email maps to many customer_id values. The selection query (lines 31-36) filters `whereNull('abandoned_email_sent_at')`, so any un-stamped duplicate is re-picked next run. Ran `vendor/bin/phpunit --filter ReservationAbandonedTest` — 10/10 pass, but no test covers same-email/different-customer_id.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M31 — UpgradeToRates command has zero test coverage despite mutating production data**
  - **Where:** `src/Console/Commands/UpgradeToRates.php:27-274`
  - **Problem:** resrv:upgrade-to-rates is a data-mutating one-shot upgrade command (it rewrites rate titles from blueprint property labels and the default rate's title) shipped for the 5->6 release, and there is no test exercising it. grep for 'upgrade-to-rates' / 'UpgradeToRates' across tests/ returns nothing; tests/Console/ contains only ImportEntriesTest.php. Regressions in processCollection()/updateStandardRate()/detectCrossEntryConnections() would only surface on a customer's production database during their upgrade. Severity is medium as a release-risk/maintainability call (note: it is a one-shot tool, not hot-path code).
  - **Fix:** Add feature tests using the existing blueprint fixtures: (1) --dry-run reports the right updatedCount and writes nothing; (2) real run renames property-slug rates to their blueprint labels; (3) re-running is idempotent (also catches finding #4); (4) cross-entry connection warnings fire for same_slug/specific_slugs/entries.
  - **Evidence:** `grep -rln 'upgrade-to-rates\|UpgradeToRates' tests/` returns no matches; `ls tests/Console/` shows only ImportEntriesTest.php. UpgradeToRates.php:128 `$rate->update(['title' => $label]);` and :164 `$rate->update(['title' => 'Standard Rate']);` mutate live data.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M32 — DataImport.prepare() uses mapWithKeys keyed by entry id — multiple CSV rows for the same entry overwrite each other**
  - **Where:** `src/Helpers/DataImport.php:55-87`
  - **Problem:** `prepare()` builds the import via `->mapWithKeys(fn ($row) => [$id => $data])` (lines 57-80) keyed by the resolved Statamic entry id. Laravel's `mapWithKeys` keeps only the last value for duplicate keys. Because `rate_id` is read per-row (`$row['rate_id']`, lines 72-74), importing multiple rates for one entry — or splitting an entry's date ranges across rows — requires multiple CSV rows with the same entry id, and all but the last are silently discarded. Result: silent data loss on multi-row-per-entry imports with no warning. Note: ProcessDataImport's own logic (Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:58-69) explicitly handles 'multiple rates exist, rate_id required' by skipping rows, showing multi-rate-per-entry is a supported scenario — but the collapse in prepare() defeats it for the multi-row case before the job ever sees those rows.
  - **Fix:** Aggregate instead of overwrite: group rows by id and concatenate their per-row data collections (or key by id+rate_id and merge in the job). At minimum reject duplicate entry ids with a clear error.
  - **Evidence:** DataImport.php:57 `->mapWithKeys(function ($row) {` ... line 80 `return [$id => $data];`. Each row produces one entry keyed by `$id`; duplicate ids overwrite. rate_id is per-row at lines 72-74. ProcessDataImportTest mocks the prepared structure directly, so this collapse is untested.
  - _bug · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **M33 — DataImport price-header parsing has no structure validation; malformed header silently imports availability for 'today'**  _(the data-corruption half was already fixed: `getDatesFromHeader()` guards missing parts and `ProcessDataImport::parseImportDate()` strictly skips blank/invalid dates. Remaining gap closed by validating each price header carries a `:date_start|date_end` range in `headersHaveCorrectFormat()`, surfacing a clear error at the confirm step.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Helpers/DataImport.php:90-98, 132-150`
  - **Problem:** `headersHaveCorrectFormat()` (lines 132-150) only checks that some header contains the substring 'price' and some contains 'availability'; it never validates the `label:date1|date2` structure. `getDatesFromHeader()` (line 92) does `explode('|', explode(':', $header)[1])`. A price header without a colon (e.g. a column literally named `price`) makes `explode(':', 'price')[1]` an undefined index (PHP warning, null); `explode('|', null)` yields `['']`; `$dates[1]` is undefined. I verified `Carbon::create('')` returns now() (got 2026-05-29 21:02:34) and `Carbon::create(null)` returns Jan-1 of the current year. So the row is upserted as availability/price for date_start=today, date_end=Jan-1, with no error surfaced. This corrupts availability data from a plausibly-malformed header.
  - **Fix:** In `headersHaveCorrectFormat()` validate each price header matches `/price.*:.+\|.+/` and parse-test both date parts, returning an error otherwise. In `getDatesFromHeader()` guard against missing parts and reject the row instead of falling back to now().
  - **Evidence:** DataImport.php:138/141 only do `strpos($header, 'price') !== false` / `strpos($header, 'availability')`. DataImport.php:92 `$dates = explode('|', explode(':', $header)[1]);` with no guard. Verified via `php -r` that `Carbon::create('')` = current datetime and `Carbon::create(null)` = Jan 1.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M34 — Affiliate attribution ignores the 'published' flag for both cookie set and reservation attribution**  _(added `Affiliate::scopePublished()` and applied it to both cookie-path lookups — `SetResrvAffiliateCookie` and `HandlesAffiliates::getAffiliateIfCookieExists()` — so disabled affiliates are neither cookied nor attributed (and so can't trigger `allow_skipping_payment`). Coupon-driven attribution is a separate path, out of scope for this finding.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Middleware/SetResrvAffiliateCookie.php:27-28`
  - **Problem:** `Affiliate::where('code', $afid)->first()` (SetResrvAffiliateCookie.php:27) does not filter on `published`; neither does `HandlesAffiliates::getAffiliateIfCookieExists()` (HandlesAffiliates.php:11 `Affiliate::where('code', request()->cookie('resrv_afid'))->first()`) nor `AddAffiliateToReservation` (which just attaches whatever affiliate the cookie resolved). The `published` boolean exists on the model (Affiliate.php:23/30, cast to boolean, default true in migration 2024_07_03_113105_create_resrv_affiliates_table.php:23) and is editable in the CP (AffiliateCpRequest.php:37), strongly implying it enables/disables an affiliate — but it is never consulted anywhere in the attribution path. So an unpublished (disabled) affiliate still gets the cookie set, still earns `fee`, and because `allow_skipping_payment` is read off the attached affiliate (Checkout.php:465 → HandlesAffiliates::affiliateCanSkipPayment, line 17), a disabled affiliate with `allow_skipping_payment=true` can still make checkouts skip payment.
  - **Fix:** Add `->where('published', true)` to the affiliate lookups in SetResrvAffiliateCookie and HandlesAffiliates (or add a `scopePublished` and use it everywhere), so disabled affiliates are neither cookied nor attributed. If `published` is meant as display-only, rename it to make that explicit.
  - **Evidence:** SetResrvAffiliateCookie.php:27 `if ($affiliate = Affiliate::where('code', $afid)->first())`. HandlesAffiliates.php:11 same pattern, no published filter. AddAffiliateToReservation.php:11-12 attaches unconditionally. Affiliate.php:23/30 declares published. Migration default true. Checkout.php:465 `if (! $this->affiliateCanSkipPayment())` reads off the attached affiliate.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M35 — Report::topSellerItems triggers N+1 entry lookups and re-filters/re-sums the full collection per item**  _(rewrote `topSellerItems()` to derive top items from the already-loaded `$this->reservations` via one `groupBy('item_id')` — this removes the redundant `getTopItems()` query, the per-item full-collection re-scans, AND aligns the status set (confirmed+partner) across count/revenue/percentage. Entries batch-resolved via the existing `ResolvesReservationEntries` concern. Kept the `Price::format()`-based in-memory sum rather than the report's SQL SUM/AVG, which would do raw float arithmetic on the `price` float column — bypassing the money abstraction and the still-open M37.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Report.php:49-67, 25`
  - **Problem:** The constructor loads the entire matching reservation set into $this->reservations via ->get() (lines 22-25). topSellerItems() (49-67), for each of up to 10 items, reads $item->entry['title']/['url'] (appended Entry::find+augment, one stache lookup per item) and runs $this->reservations->where('item_id',...)->sum(closure) and ->avg(closure) — each walking the full in-memory collection again and calling $reservation->price->format() (Price cast + moneyphp format) per element. The mismatch the reviewer flagged is also real and worth fixing: getTopItems() (84-95) filters status='confirmed' ONLY, while the constructor collection (and thus the per-item sum/avg/percentage denominator via countConfirmedReservations()) includes both 'confirmed' and 'partner' (line 24). So percentage and per-item totals are computed over different status sets. Medium severity is right — only material on large date ranges.
  - **Fix:** Compute per-item COUNT/SUM/AVG in a single GROUP BY item_id aggregate (ORDER BY count DESC LIMIT 10) instead of re-scanning the in-memory collection 2× per item. Batch-resolve the 10 entry titles via one lookup (or a per-request entry cache). Align the status filter: either include 'partner' in getTopItems() or restrict the constructor collection to match, so percentage denominators and per-item sums use the same set.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 22-25: constructor `->whereIn('status', ['confirmed','partner'])->get()`. Lines 55-60: `$this->reservations->where('item_id', $item->item_id)->sum(fn ... $reservation->price->format())` and the same for ->avg() — two full-collection passes per item. Line 52 `$item->entry['title']` (appended accessor). getTopItems() line 90 `->where('status', 'confirmed')` (single status) vs constructor's two-status whereIn driving countConfirmedReservations() used at line 61.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: affiliate-customer-data sweep(s)_

### Mail / Support / Providers

- [x] **M36 — searchJson tag emits json_encode without HTML-safe flags, enabling reflected XSS**  _(fixed by adding `JSON_HEX_TAG | JSON_HEX_AMP | JSON_HEX_APOS | JSON_HEX_QUOT` to the encode. Note the finding's premise is overstated: PHP's default `json_encode` **does** escape `/`→`\/`, so the canonical `</script>` breakout in a `<script>` block is already blocked — `<\/script>` isn't a valid close tag. The flags are still correct hardening: they make the output safe in other contexts (HTML attributes) and remove reliance on fragile slash-escaping. Skipped the suggested middleware input-validation as disproportionate for a medium issue — the tag's output is the correct trust boundary and is now safe regardless of session contents.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Tags/Resrv.php:14-21`
  - **Problem:** Resrv::searchJson() returns json_encode(session()->get('resrv_search')) with no flags. The session payload is built from raw, unvalidated GET params (date_start/date_end/duration/quantity/rate_id) via $request->only([...]) in SetResrvSearchByVariables::handle() (line 26) and persisted verbatim by SaveSearchToSession (session(['resrv_search' => $event->data])). Default json_encode does NOT escape <, >, &, /, so a value like ?date_start=</script><script>... would break out of a <script> block. Statamic Antlers does not HTML-escape tag output, and the *_json naming plus its return shape strongly imply consumers embed it in a <script> block, which is the canonical use for such a tag. This is a real XSS vector. Correcting the original 'stored/reflected' framing: it is reflected and self-stored in the victim's OWN session (an attacker must lure the victim to a crafted URL); it is not cross-user persistent XSS, hence medium rather than high.
  - **Fix:** Encode with HTML-safe flags: json_encode(session()->get('resrv_search'), JSON_HEX_TAG | JSON_HEX_AMP | JSON_HEX_APOS | JSON_HEX_QUOT). Additionally validate/whitelist the params at write time in SetResrvSearchByVariables (date-shaped date_start/date_end, integer quantity/rate_id) so non-conforming values never reach the session.
  - **Evidence:** Line 20: `return json_encode(session()->get('resrv_search'));` (no flags). SetResrvSearchByVariables.php line 26: `$data = collect($request->only(['date_start', 'date_end', 'duration', 'quantity', 'rate_id']));` then `AvailabilitySearch::dispatch($data->toArray());` with no validation. SaveSearchToSession.php line 11: `session(['resrv_search' => $event->data]);` stores it verbatim. No test exercises the tag's output escaping.
  - _security · confirmed · medium confidence_

### Database / Migrations

- [x] **M37 — Money price stored in a FLOAT column (float(8,2)) — precision loss and value overflow**
  - **Fixed:** Added migration `2026_06_02_000000_change_fixed_pricing_price_to_decimal.php` converting `resrv_fixed_pricing.price` from float to `decimal(10,2)` (pgsql raw `ALTER ... TYPE ... USING price::decimal(10,2)`, else `->change()` — same pattern as the existing `fix_*_column_type` migrations), matching the rate-table convention (`resrv_rates.modifier_amount`, `resrv_child_reservations.price`). Also changed the legacy column re-created by `finalize_rate_migration` down() (line 141) to decimal. **Independent-review correction:** the report's "`bcmul($float,100)` truncates" mechanism is outdated — the H7 fix already rewrote `Price::create()` to use moneyphp's `DecimalMoneyParser`, so that specific truncation is gone. But the core defect stands and matters *more* post-H7: with 0-/3-decimal currencies now supported (JPY/BHD/KWD), a `float(8,2)` column can't hold 3-decimal precision and caps magnitude (~999,999.99 on MySQL). No code change needed in `FixedPricing.php` — both the cast and the raw `DB::table()` read pass the value through `Price::create()`, which handles a decimal string. **Scope:** fixed exactly M37's documented column; the same float→money pattern exists in other older tables (reservations/availabilities/extras/options/etc.) but those aren't in this finding and a full sweep is a separate, larger migration. **Test:** `test_price_column_is_stored_as_decimal_not_float` asserts the column reports decimal/numeric (verified it returns `numeric` post-fix vs `float` for the unchanged `reservations.price`, so it has teeth). A functional precision test is impossible on the SQLite/Postgres suite because SQLite collapses both to REAL affinity. The pgsql branch couldn't be executed here (`pdo_pgsql` absent + no running server) but the SQL is standard and matches the tested `fix_child_reservation_id_column_type` precedent.
  - **Where:** `database/migrations/2021_06_10_100619_create_fixed_pricing_table.php:20`
  - **Problem:** resrv_fixed_pricing.price is `$table->float('price', 8, 2)`, and the rate-migration down() (2026_03_01_000004_finalize_rate_migration.php:141) re-creates the legacy advanced-availabilities column as float too. Money everywhere else flows through Price (moneyphp) precisely to avoid IEEE-754 error, yet the canonical fixed-price value is persisted as a float. getFixedPricing() (FixedPricing.php scopeGetFixedPricing) reads rows via raw `DB::table('resrv_fixed_pricing')->get()` (stdClass, so $item->price is the raw float) and feeds it to Price::create() -> bcmul($float, 100), which truncates rather than rounds. On MySQL a FLOAT round-trip like 77.34999998 truncates to 7734 cents (1-cent error); float(8,2) also caps magnitude at ~999999.99. This is the exact 'never store money as float' anti-pattern the rest of the system avoids. Note: the test suite runs on SQLite/Postgres where SQLite stores REAL and the typical impact is smaller, which is why it is medium not high.
  - **Fix:** Change the column to integer minor units or `decimal('price', 10, 2)`, consistent with how other money is handled, and read via getRawOriginal where raw queries are used. At minimum decimal(10,2) removes binary float error.
  - **Evidence:** Migration line 20: `$table->float('price', 8, 2);`. finalize_rate_migration.php:141 (down): `$table->float('price', 8, 2);`. FixedPricing.php scopeGetFixedPricing does `DB::table('resrv_fixed_pricing')->get()` then `Price::create($items->where('days', $days)->first()->price)`. I confirmed bcmul truncation: bcmul('77.34999998',100)=7734.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **M38 — No composite index for reservation overlap queries on (rate_id, status, date_start, date_end)**
  - **Fixed:** Added migration `2026_06_02_000001_add_overlap_indexes_to_reservations.php` creating a composite index on `resrv_reservations` and `resrv_child_reservations` (custom-named, matching the `resrv_avail_search_idx` convention). **Refined the report's column set:** I used `(rate_id, date_start, date_end)`, *omitting* `status`. The report proposed `(rate_id, status, date_start, date_end)`, but `status` is queried as `whereNotIn('status', terminal())` — a set-negation a b-tree can't range-seek, and placing it before the date range fragments the scan. With it dropped, the index seeks on `rate_id =`, range-scans `date_start`, filters `date_end` in-index, and `status` stays a cheap post-filter on the narrowed set. The child table never filters status directly (it comes via the `whereHas('parent')` EXISTS), so `(rate_id, date_start, date_end)` is exactly right there. **Scope trims (proportionate for a medium/medium-confidence perf finding):** skipped the report's speculative `(status, date_start)` calendar/report index (not among the four cited query sites), and skipped an `item_id`-led index for `ActiveReservationsGuard::hasActiveReservationsForRange` (admin-CP-only, and the existing single-column `item_id` index already narrows to the entry before the date filter). **Verification:** indexes are additive and don't change results, so a functional regression test can't observe them — added `test_composite_overlap_indexes_exist_on_reservation_tables` (schema introspection via `Schema::getIndexes`, exact column-order match). Relevant suites green (93 tests / 206 assertions across `RateSharedAvailabilityTest` + `AvailabilityMultiResultsTest`). The report's `EXPLAIN`-on-Postgres validation (and any further column-order tuning) couldn't be run here — `pdo_pgsql` is absent and no PG server is up — so it's left for the maintainer; the chosen order follows standard equality-then-range b-tree design.
  - **Where:** `database/migrations/2026_03_01_000002_add_rate_id_to_existing_tables.php:10-26`
  - **Problem:** The hot overlap/capacity queries filter resrv_reservations / resrv_child_reservations by rate_id + status + date_start < ? + date_end > ?: validateMaxAvailableForDateRange (AvailabilityRepository 371-387), getExhaustedDatesForRates (329-335), validateMaxAvailableForDemand (HandlesAvailabilityQueries 285-295) and ActiveReservationsGuard::hasActiveReservationsForRange (33-51). The schema only has single-column indexes (status, item_id, rate_id from this migration). A b-tree can use only the leading column of one index per scan, so these range-overlap checks scan a large slice and filter the rest. Some run inside checkout under lockForUpdate and on availability searches, so they are latency-sensitive. Confirmed; medium (index absence only bites once the reservations table is large).
  - **Fix:** Add composite indexes via a new migration: resrv_reservations (rate_id, status, date_start, date_end), (status, date_start) for calendar/report range scans, and resrv_child_reservations (rate_id, date_start, date_end). Validate with EXPLAIN on Postgres (per CLAUDE.md). Order leading columns by equality-first (rate_id, status) then range (date_start) for best b-tree usage.
  - **Evidence:** Migration only declares `$table->index('rate_id');` per table (lines 13, 18, 23). AvailabilityRepository 371-376 `Reservation::where('rate_id', $rate->id)->whereNotIn('status', ...)->where('date_start','<',$dateEnd)->where('date_end','>',$dateStart)`. ActiveReservationsGuard 33-38 same shape with item_id+status+date range. No composite index exists for these.
  - _performance · confirmed · medium confidence_

## 🟡 Low (107)

### Payments & Webhooks

- [x] **L1 — Confirmed/terminal short-circuits run before signature verification (pre-auth DB probe)**
  - **Fixed:** Moved the already-CONFIRMED status short-circuit to *after* `Webhook::constructEvent`, and re-derive `$data = $event->data->object` from the verified event before any state handling. A forged/unsigned webhook now aborts 403 at verification and can no longer observe a reservation's CONFIRMED status (the status oracle the report flagged). **Independent-review nuance:** the report's literal prescription ("move constructEvent to the top, then do *all* lookups on trusted data") can't be fully followed — `getWebhookSecret($reservation)` resolves a *per-collection* secret from `$reservation->entry()->collection`, so the reservation lookup must run *before* verification to pick the right secret. The lookup therefore stays first (its result isn't acted on until the signature verifies); the residual is a weak reservation-existence probe inherent to per-collection-secret webhooks, far below the status oracle that's now closed. **Scope:** L1 only. The dead `Event::constructFrom` block (L2) and the `$_SERVER['HTTP_STRIPE_SIGNATURE']` superglobal read (L3) sit in the same method but are separate findings handled in their own iterations — leaving L3 also keeps the existing test signing helper (which sets `$_SERVER`) working unchanged. **Tests:** updated `test_verify_payment_short_circuits_for_already_confirmed_reservation` to send a *signed* request (now asserts real idempotency: 200 + no re-confirm) and added `test_verify_payment_verifies_signature_before_confirmed_short_circuit` (forged request → 403; verified it has teeth — on the old ordering it returned 200). Full webhook suite green (16 tests / 56 assertions) plus `MultiplePaymentCheckoutTest` (12/32).
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:211-230`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed: verifyPayment decodes the UNVERIFIED payload (207-209), looks up the reservation by attacker-controlled $data['id'] (211) and the unverified $data['metadata']['reservation_id'] (217-219), and returns 200 for an already-CONFIRMED reservation (228-230) — all before signature verification at line 244. I ran test_verify_payment_short_circuits_for_already_confirmed_reservation: it passes with a plain Request carrying no Stripe-Signature header, proving the 200 is returned without any signature check. No state changes occur in this region so impact is limited to an unauthenticated DB-lookup probe and a status oracle (confirmed-vs-other observable via response/timing) using attacker-supplied ids. Low severity but the ordering is genuinely backwards.
  - **Fix:** Move Webhook::constructEvent(...) to the top of verifyPayment, derive $data from the verified $event->data->object, then perform reservation lookups and status short-circuits on trusted data.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 207-211 decode and look up on the raw payload; 217-219 use unverified metadata; 228-230 `if ($reservation->status === CONFIRMED) return response()->json([],200);` — all above the constructEvent at 244. Targeted test (StripeWebhookTest::test_verify_payment_short_circuits_for_already_confirmed_reservation) PASSED with an unsigned request, confirming pre-verification execution.
  - _security · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-concurrency sweep(s)_

- [x] **L2 — Dead/duplicated pre-verification Event::constructFrom on the unverified payload**
  - **Fixed:** Deleted the dead `try { $event = Event::constructFrom(...) } catch (\UnexpectedValueException)` block and the now-unused `use Stripe\Event;` import (confirmed `Event::` had no other usage in the file). Verified safe: `$event` is reassigned by the verified `Webhook::constructEvent` before any use, and the deleted catch caught root-namespace `\UnexpectedValueException` (which `constructFrom` doesn't throw) — distinct from the `Stripe\Exception\UnexpectedValueException` caught at the verified block, whose import is retained. Pure dead-code removal with no behavioral change, so no new test — the existing webhook suite (16 tests / 56 assertions) regression-covers it; Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:234-239`
  - **Problem:** Lines 234-239 build `$event = Event::constructFrom(json_decode($request->getContent(), true))` from the UNVERIFIED payload and immediately overwrite it with the signature-verified Webhook::constructEvent(...) at 244-250. The first block is dead work: it implies validation it does not actually perform, catches the global \UnexpectedValueException (236) while the verified call catches Stripe\Exception\UnexpectedValueException (254) — two different classes — and decodes the body an additional time (already decoded at 207, and again inside constructEvent at 245). Safe to delete.
  - **Fix:** Delete lines 234-239; rely solely on the verified Webhook::constructEvent at 244-250 as the single source of $event.
  - **Evidence:** Line 235 `$event = Event::constructFrom(json_decode($request->getContent(), true));` then line 244 reassigns `$event = Webhook::constructEvent(...)`. Import at top: line 17 `use Stripe\Exception\UnexpectedValueException;`, but the try block at 236 catches `\UnexpectedValueException` (root namespace) — distinct from the Stripe one caught at 254.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-security sweep(s)_

- [x] **L3 — Stripe signature header read via raw $_SERVER superglobal, breaking on missing header**
  - **Fixed:** Replaced `$sig_header = $_SERVER['HTTP_STRIPE_SIGNATURE']` with `$request->header('Stripe-Signature')` and added an explicit `if (empty($sig_header)) { abort(403); }` before `constructEvent`. This removes the "Undefined array key" warning on a missing header and avoids passing `null` into `Webhook::constructEvent` (a possible TypeError uncaught by the signature/payload catches), while still ending at 403 for unsigned requests. **Test alignment:** the signing helper now passes the HMAC via the `Request::create` `$server` arg (`HTTP_STRIPE_SIGNATURE`, which Symfony lands in the request header bag) instead of mutating the `$_SERVER` superglobal; the obsolete `tearDown` that cleaned that global was removed (no global state is touched now). The unsigned-webhook test now exercises the new empty-header guard (missing `Stripe-Signature` → 403), and the signed tests prove `$request->header()` reads the header correctly. Full `tests/Payment` suite green (98 tests / 219 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:241`
  - **Problem:** Line 241 reads `$sig_header = $_SERVER['HTTP_STRIPE_SIGNATURE'];` directly from the superglobal rather than the injected $request. If the header is absent (any non-Stripe/forged POST that gets past the earlier short-circuits), PHP emits an 'Undefined array key' warning and $sig_header is null. The flow still ends at abort(403) because getTimestamp() returns -1 on a null/empty header, but the warning pollutes logs and bypasses the framework request abstraction (header-casing normalization, proxies, testability). Minor but valid.
  - **Fix:** Use `$sig_header = $request->header('Stripe-Signature');` and `if (empty($sig_header)) { abort(403); }` before constructEvent.
  - **Evidence:** Line 241 verbatim: `$sig_header = $_SERVER['HTTP_STRIPE_SIGNATURE'];`. verifyPayment already receives `$request` (line 205) and uses `$request->getContent()` elsewhere (207, 245), so the superglobal access is gratuitous.
  - _best-practice · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-security, xc-concurrency sweep(s)_

- [x] **L4 — Stripe webhook does not validate the charged amount against the reservation total**
  - **Fixed:** Added an amount guard on the verified `payment_intent.succeeded` branch, just before `transitionTo(CONFIRMED)`: compute the owed total in minor units (`$reservation->payment->add($reservation->payment_surcharge)->raw()` — the same value `initializePayment` charges) and, when the event carries `amount_received`, refuse to confirm on a mismatch — log a warning and dispatch `OrphanedPaymentNotification` instead (reusing the pattern already used twice in this method for stale/terminal orphans). **Independent-review note:** kept minimal and defense-in-depth only, matching the verifier's downgrade to low — the common path is already safe (intent created server-side with the correct total; amount-affecting changes clear `payment_id`). The check is `isset`-guarded on `amount_received` so it enforces for real Stripe succeeded events (which always include it) without disturbing the amount-less test payloads. Used `payment->add(payment_surcharge)->raw()` rather than `totalToCharge()` because the latter returns a formatted decimal string. Scope: Stripe gateway only (`FakePaymentGateway` carries no charged amount). **Tests:** added `test_verify_payment_does_not_confirm_when_charged_amount_differs_from_reservation_total` (mismatch → stays PENDING, no `ReservationConfirmed`, orphan email sent) and `test_verify_payment_confirms_when_charged_amount_matches_reservation_total` (matching amount still confirms, no orphan email); extended the `signedWebhookRequest` helper with an optional object-data arg. Full `tests/Payment` suite green (100 tests / 227 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:259-303`
  - **Problem:** On payment_intent.succeeded the reservation is transitioned to CONFIRMED with no comparison of the intent's amount_received/amount against what the reservation owes (totalToCharge() = payment + payment_surcharge). The common path is safe because initializePayment() creates the intent server-side with the correct $totalToCharge, and a coupon/gateway/surcharge change in Checkout cancels the old intent and clears payment_id (the stale-intent branch then catches the abandoned charge). So the described exploit requires an attacker who can both keep payment_id matching and substitute a different-amount intent that Stripe still reports as succeeded under that id — not generally achievable. The finding is therefore better framed as missing defense-in-depth rather than an exploitable bug; severity downgraded to low.
  - **Fix:** Optional hardening: on the succeeded branch compare $data['amount_received'] against $reservation->totalToCharge() in minor units (Price::create(...)->raw()); on mismatch log + dispatch OrphanedPaymentNotification and do not confirm.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 259-303 handle payment_intent.succeeded and call transitionTo(CONFIRMED) with no amount check. Checkout.php:417 creates the intent with the server-computed $totalToCharge, and cancelActiveIntent clears payment_id on amount-affecting changes (the stale-intent branch at 266-277 is the only amount-mismatch guard, keyed on cleared payment_id, not on a numeric comparison).
  - _security · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L5 — Duplicate succeeded webhooks for a terminal/stale reservation re-send orphan-payment emails (no idempotency)**
  - **Fixed:** Added a cache-based "notify once" guard inside the shared `OrphanedPaymentNotification::dispatchFor()` — the single entry point used by both Stripe orphan branches (stale + terminal) and the FakeGateway, so all call sites and any future gateway get dedup from one change. Keyed on `(reservation_id, payment_intent_id)` (stable across Stripe's redeliveries and available in both gateways now, without depending on L6's event id): `Cache::has()` short-circuits a repeat, and the marker is set with `Cache::put(..., now()->addDays(4))` (comfortably past Stripe's ~3-day retry window) **only when `send()` returns true**, so a disabled/no-recipient/failed run doesn't permanently suppress a genuine later notification. **Independent-review note:** rejected the report's heavier "persist a marker" (DB column/table) option as disproportionate for admin-email noise (low severity) — the cache guard is ~6 lines, no migration, and idiomatic. Per-recipient fan-out within a single delivery is unchanged (the existing two-admins test still sends 2). **Tests:** added `test_duplicate_orphan_webhook_only_notifies_admins_once` (two identical orphan webhooks → exactly one email); the array cache store is per-test so there's no cross-test bleed. Full `tests/Payment` suite green (101 tests / 229 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:266-297`
  - **Problem:** Both the stale-intent branch (266-277) and the terminal-state branch (283-297) call OrphanedPaymentNotification::dispatchFor(...) and return 200 with no persisted idempotency marker. Stripe retries webhooks for up to ~3 days and can deliver duplicates, so an orphan charge against a terminal/stale reservation generates a fresh admin email on every redelivery. The dispatcher also fans out one mail per admin recipient (test test_orphan_notification_sends_one_message_per_admin_recipient asserts 2 mails for 2 admins), multiplying the spam. The same gap exists in FakePaymentGateway (lines 162-175). Note the genuine confirm path IS idempotent (the CONFIRMED short-circuit at 228 plus transitionTo() no-op, proven by test_fake_gateway_duplicate_succeeded_webhook_is_idempotent); only the orphan path lacks dedup. Real but low severity (admin email noise, not data corruption).
  - **Fix:** Persist a marker that an orphan notification was sent for a (reservation_id, payment_intent_id) or Stripe event id, and skip dispatchFor if already recorded; at minimum dedupe on the Stripe event id (also see finding about passing $event->id).
  - **Evidence:** Lines 274 and 294 both unconditionally call `OrphanedPaymentNotification::dispatchFor($reservation, $data['id'])` then `return response()->json([], 200)`. No idempotency column/cache exists. tests/Payment/StripeWebhookTest.php:140-158 confirms one mail per admin per invocation; there is a duplicate-confirm idempotency test (179-196) but none for duplicate orphan webhooks.
  - _bug · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L6 — Stripe gateway never passes the Stripe event id to the orphan notification**
  - **Fixed:** Passed the verified event id as the third arg to every orphan dispatch — `OrphanedPaymentNotification::dispatchFor($reservation, $data['id'], $event->id ?? null)` — so the email template's "Event id" line now renders for the real gateway, giving admins the reconciliation handle. Applied to all **three** orphan branches (stale-intent, terminal-state, and the amount-mismatch branch added in L4), not just the two the report cited, since they all benefit from the same handle. **Independent-review note:** used `$event->id ?? null` (the form the report proposed) rather than a bare `$event->id`: `??` resolves via `StripeObject::__isset` first, so an event lacking an `id` yields null silently instead of emitting Stripe's "Undefined property" SDK notice (which surfaced in test output with the bare access). Trivial one-arg change, clearly worth it for a usability nit. **Tests:** added `test_stripe_orphan_notification_includes_the_verified_event_id` (signed succeeded webhook carrying a top-level `evt_...` id to a terminal reservation → asserts the dispatched `OrphanedPaymentNotification->stripeEventId` matches); extended the `signedWebhookRequest` helper with an optional top-level event-id arg. Full `tests/Payment` suite green (102 tests / 231 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:274, 294`
  - **Problem:** OrphanedPaymentNotification accepts an optional $stripeEventId (constructor param, used by the email template orphaned-payment.blade.php lines 13-14 to render 'Event id'). StripePaymentGateway calls dispatchFor($reservation, $data['id']) at both 274 and 294 with only the payment intent id, omitting the verified event id ($event->id is available after constructEvent). So the template's event-id branch never renders for the real gateway, and admins lose the most useful reconciliation/idempotency handle. Confirmed maintainability/usability nit.
  - **Fix:** Pass the verified event id in both orphan branches: `OrphanedPaymentNotification::dispatchFor($reservation, $data['id'], $event->id ?? null);`.
  - **Evidence:** Mail/OrphanedPaymentNotification.php:25 `public ?string $stripeEventId = null` and dispatchFor signature at :39 accepts it. Template orphaned-payment.blade.php:13-14 `@if ($stripeEventId) ... Event id ... @endif`. Gateway lines 274 and 294 call dispatchFor with only `$data['id']`, never `$event->id`.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L7 — Stripe::setApiKey uses SDK global static — wrong key under Octane / per-collection multisite keys**
  - **Fixed:** Standardized every Stripe call on per-instance `StripeClient` (matching `handleRedirectBack`, which already did): `paymentIntent()` → `$stripe->paymentIntents->create(...)`, `cancelPaymentIntent()` → `$stripe->paymentIntents->retrieve(...)` + `->cancel($paymentId)`, `refund()` → `$stripe->refunds->create(...)`. Dropped all four `Stripe::setApiKey()` global-static mutations and the now-unused `Stripe`, `PaymentIntent`, `Refund` imports. **Independent-review note:** the `Stripe::setApiKey` in `verifyPayment` was vestigial — its only SDK call (`Webhook::constructEvent`) uses the *webhook secret*, not the API key, and the canceled→`expire()` path resolves the gateway via `PaymentGatewayManager` and calls `cancelPaymentIntent` (which sets its own key), so removing it changes nothing in FPM while closing the cross-request key-leak window under Octane + multisite per-collection key arrays. Mechanical transformation, no new code/dependencies — proportionate for a low/best-practice item. Exception handling is unchanged (instance methods throw the same `Stripe\Exception\*` hierarchy the catch blocks already handle). Confirmed no code outside the gateway uses Stripe SDK statics or `getApiKey`. **Tests:** added `test_verify_payment_does_not_mutate_the_global_stripe_api_key` (seeds a sentinel global key, runs a signed succeeded webhook, asserts the global is untouched and the reservation still confirms — verified it has teeth: the old line-223 `setApiKey` made it 'sk_test'). The create/retrieve/refund methods remain SDK-boundary calls the suite intentionally doesn't hit over the network. Full `tests/Payment` suite green (103 tests / 233 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:43, 58, 76, 232`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed that paymentIntent (43), cancelPaymentIntent (58), refund (76) and verifyPayment (232) call the process-global Stripe::setApiKey($this->getSecretKey($reservation)), while handleRedirectBack (174) uses an instance `new StripeClient($secret)` — an inconsistent mix. The leak risk is real only for multisite per-collection key arrays under a persistent worker (Octane) or shared-process concurrency; in standard FPM each request sets the key before its own SDK call within the same synchronous flow, so a single reservation's key is correct for that request. There is no concurrency inside one verifyPayment/paymentIntent call. So this is a latent fragility/best-practice issue (and a real risk under Octane + multisite array keys), not a demonstrated bug in the default deployment; severity downgraded to low.
  - **Fix:** Standardize on instance clients: `$stripe = new StripeClient($this->getSecretKey($reservation));` then `$stripe->paymentIntents->create/retrieve/cancel(...)`, `$stripe->refunds->create(...)`; drop the global Stripe::setApiKey calls.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 43, 58, 76, 232 each `Stripe::setApiKey($this->getSecretKey($reservation));` (global static). Line 174 `$stripe = new StripeClient($this->getSecretKey($reservation));` uses an instance, proving the inconsistency. getSecretKey (111-121) supports an array keyed by collection handle, which is the multisite case where a leaked global key would target the wrong Stripe account.
  - _bug · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L8 — Customer data forwarded to Stripe metadata without length/key-count limits — PaymentIntent::create can throw**
  - **Fixed:** Clamped `filterCustomerData()` to Stripe's documented metadata limits at the source: keep only string values whose key is ≤ 40 chars, `take(49)` (so the caller's merged-in `reservation_id` keeps the total ≤ 50 keys), and `mb_substr($value, 0, 500)` each value. This removes the exact trigger for the uncaught `InvalidRequestException` on `create()` in ~5 lines. **Independent-review note:** deliberately scoped down from the report's fuller proposal. (1) Skipped wrapping `create()` in a try/catch — a "clean checkout error" requires deciding user-facing behavior and integrating with the Checkout flow, disproportionate for a low/conditional item, and the clamp already eliminates the documented metadata-limit failure mode. (2) Did not strip PII fields ("consider only sending reservation_id…") — changing *what* data is forwarded is a product decision with downstream reconciliation impact (admins rely on customer data in the dashboard); enforcing the limits keeps current behaviour safe without that risk. Dropped over-long keys rather than truncating them (truncation could collide two distinct handles to the same 40-char key). Used char-based `mb_*` (Stripe counts characters, and form values may be multibyte). **Tests:** added `tests/Payment/StripePaymentGatewayTest.php` — its natural home vs. the webhook-named file — with `test_filter_customer_data_clamps_values_keys_and_non_strings_to_stripe_limits` (600-char value → 500, 41-char key dropped, non-string dropped) and `test_filter_customer_data_caps_key_count_below_stripe_limit` (60 fields → ≤ 49), invoking the protected method via reflection (offline, no SDK mock). Full `tests/Payment` suite green (105 tests / 239 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Payment/StripePaymentGateway.php:44-51, 89-97`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed that filterCustomerData() (89-97) forwards every string customer field into PaymentIntent metadata (47), and paymentIntent() has no try/catch, so a value exceeding Stripe's metadata limits (50 keys, key ≤ 40 chars, value ≤ 500 chars) would raise an uncaught InvalidRequestException and break checkout. The customer data is the checkout form payload (Checkout.php:417 passes $reservation->customerData), which can contain free-text fields. Whether limits are actually exceeded depends entirely on the site's checkout blueprint (field handles ≤ 40 chars, value lengths), so this is a conditional/defensive issue rather than a guaranteed bug, and the PII point (full name/email/address copied into Stripe metadata) is a valid privacy nit. Severity low, conditional on site config.
  - **Fix:** In filterCustomerData truncate each value to 500 chars, cap forwarded keys (and key length to 40), and consider only sending reservation_id plus essential identifiers; wrap PaymentIntent::create in try/catch that surfaces a clean checkout error instead of an unhandled exception.
  - **Evidence:** filterCustomerData (89-97) only filters `is_string($value)` with no length/count cap; line 47 merges it into 'metadata'. paymentIntent (41-54) has no try/catch around PaymentIntent::create. Checkout.php:417 feeds it `$reservation->customerData` (the user-entered form collection).
  - _bug · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

### Reservations & State machine

- [x] **L9 — findByPaymentId scope matches all reservations with empty/cleared payment_id**
  - **Fixed:** Guarded the scope at the root so a falsy id matches nothing: `where('payment_id', $id)->where('payment_id', '!=', '')->whereNotNull('payment_id')`. When `$id` is `''` the first two clauses contradict (empty set); when `$id` is `null` Laravel's null-shortcut turns it into `whereNull('payment_id')` which contradicts the `whereNotNull` — so both falsy cases resolve to no rows, while a real `pi_…` id still matches (the extra clauses are redundant-but-harmless on the happy path). **Independent-review note:** fixed the scope rather than adding an `empty($data['id'])` bail in `verifyPayment` only — the scope is the root and protects *both* consumers (`verifyPayment` and `handleRedirectBack`) plus any future caller in one place. Confirmed valid-but-not-currently-reachable (signature verification now precedes state changes after the H1/L1–L3 work, and real Stripe events carry non-empty ids), so this is defensive low hardening. Declarative form (no early-return / `whereRaw('1=0')` hack); SQL is portable (plain `!=`/`IS NOT NULL`, verified by inspection — same on SQLite/Postgres, no JSON/sequence quirks). **Tests:** added `test_find_by_payment_id_ignores_reservations_with_a_cleared_payment_id` to `StateMachineTest` (its natural home — payment_id clearing is an expire() side effect): an empty id returns null despite a cleared `''` reservation existing, while a real id still resolves. Verified teeth (pre-fix it returned the cleared row). `StateMachineTest` (20), plus both consumers via `StripeWebhookTest`+`ResrvCheckoutRedirectTest` (24) green; Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:160-163`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed that scopeFindByPaymentId is a plain `where('payment_id', $id)` with no empty-id guard, and expire()/cancelActiveIntent set payment_id to '' (empty string). A webhook whose data.object.id is '' would match an arbitrary cleared reservation via findByPaymentId('')->first(). In the current Stripe flow this is gated: signature verification (244-250) runs before any state change, and a real Stripe succeeded/canceled event always carries a non-empty pi_ id, so the empty-id collision is not reachable in practice today. It is unsafe-by-default and becomes exploitable only in combination with the empty-secret issue (finding 2). Defensive low-severity hardening.
  - **Fix:** Bail early in verifyPayment when `empty($data['id'])`, and/or make the scope reject falsy keys, e.g. `$query->where('payment_id', $id)->where('payment_id', '!=', '')->whereNotNull('payment_id')`.
  - **Evidence:** Reservation.php:160-163 `scopeFindByPaymentId($query, $id) { return $query->where('payment_id', $id); }`. Comments at 213-215 confirm cancelActiveIntent clears payment_id; gateway uses `Reservation::findByPaymentId($data['id'])->first()` at line 211 with no empty check on $data['id'].
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L10 — transitionTo() can throw InvalidStateTransition under a status race; webhook/Checkout callers don't catch it**
  - **Fixed:** Added a `bool $tolerant = false` parameter to `transitionTo()`. In tolerant mode, when the freshly-locked state can no longer reach the target it logs (`Log::info` with from/to/id) and returns `false` instead of throwing — turning the race into the same idempotent no-op the callers already handle. Opted in the five reactive callers (`StripePaymentGateway`, `FakePaymentGateway`, `CheckoutPayment`, and both `Checkout` confirm paths — PARTNER + zero-payment CONFIRMED) with `tolerant: true`; left `ReservationCpController::refund()` on the default so it keeps catching `InvalidStateTransition` to show the admin a 400. **Independent-review note:** chose the report's "tolerant mode" option over wrapping each call site in try/catch — the race logic lives in one place, every reactive caller opts in with a single named arg, and future callers get a clear knob. Verified all five reactive `if (transitionTo(...)) { dispatch }` bodies are pure event-dispatch followed by a redirect/200, so a `false` return is safe (skips the dispatch, proceeds). Since `transitionTo` always re-reads `$fresh` under the lock and decides on that value alone, a pre-set terminal reservation exercises the identical code path as a real concurrent flip — no need to simulate true concurrency. The rare orphan-in-race (charge succeeded, row expired in the window) is accepted per the finding's "log + no-op" framing; the existing terminal-state orphan branch still covers the non-racy case. **Tests:** added `test_tolerant_transition_returns_false_instead_of_throwing_on_invalid_transition` to `StateMachineTest` (the default-throws path is already covered by `test_expired_to_confirmed_is_rejected`). Ran `StateMachineTest` (21), full `tests/Payment`, and the `Checkout`/`CheckoutPayment` Livewire suites — 154 tests / 408 assertions green; Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:172-194`
  - **Problem:** transitionTo() re-reads the row under lockForUpdate and re-validates against canTransitionTo, throwing InvalidStateTransition if the state changed since the caller's in-memory pre-check. The CP refund() path catches it (ReservationCpController.php:223-227), but the webhook/Checkout paths do not. In StripePaymentGateway::verifyPayment, the succeeded branch pre-checks $reservation->status against terminal states (lines 283-297) using the in-memory value, then calls transitionTo(CONFIRMED) at line 299; WebhookController::store() (line 23) invokes verifyPayment with no try/catch around InvalidStateTransition. So if a concurrent expire() flips PENDING->EXPIRED between the pre-check and the lock, transitionTo throws, the exception propagates out of the webhook and returns HTTP 500, prompting Stripe retries. Same uncaught pattern at FakePaymentGateway.php:177/188, CheckoutPayment.php:80, Checkout.php:473/489. No data corruption — it's a noisy-500/retry-churn concern in a narrow race window, so low severity is right.
  - **Fix:** Wrap the transitionTo() calls in webhook/Checkout paths in try/catch (InvalidStateTransition) and treat as an idempotent no-op (log + return 200). Alternatively add a 'tolerant' mode to transitionTo that returns false instead of throwing when the locked state can no longer reach the target.
  - **Evidence:** transitionTo (172-194) throws InvalidStateTransition at line 184. StripePaymentGateway pre-check uses in-memory $reservation->status (283-297) then transitionTo at 299 with no surrounding try/catch (grep: try/catch in that file are around Stripe API calls, lines 60/77/234/243, not the transition). WebhookController.php:23 `$payment->verifyPayment($request);` unguarded. Other unguarded callers: FakePaymentGateway 177/188, CheckoutPayment 80, Checkout 473/489. Only ReservationCpController 224 wraps it.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-concurrency sweep(s)_

- [x] **L11 — Reservation::duration() mutates the cached date_start/date_end Carbon objects**
  - **Fixed:** Added `->copy()` before each `startOfDay()` so `duration()` no longer mutates the Carbon instances it reads, matching the sibling `HandlesAvailabilityDates::checkMinimumDate`. **Independent-review note — reported impact refuted, applied as consistency/defensive hardening:** the finding's core claim (that the zeroed time "silently persists for the rest of the request" on the model's *cached* dates) is **not reproducible in this Laravel version**. For a plain `'datetime'` cast, `HasAttributes::transformModelValue` → `castAttribute` → `asDateTime()` re-parses a *fresh* Carbon from the raw string on every `$this->date_start` access — there is no memoization (`attributeCastCache` is only for class-castable / `Attribute`-return-type accessors, not primitive datetime casts). I verified both by reading the framework source and empirically: a regression test asserting the times survive `duration()` **passes on the unmodified code**. Combined with the confirmed zero call-sites, there is no observable bug today. The `->copy()` is still worth its ~2-token cost: it removes a genuine mutable-Carbon footgun, aligns with the established convention, and future-proofs against a switch to a caching accessor. **Tests:** kept `test_duration_does_not_mutate_the_cached_dates` as a forward-looking behavioral guard (asserts the 3-day result and that both endpoints retain their time component); it documents the side-effect-free contract even though it cannot fail against today's non-memoizing cast. `StateMachineTest` green (22 tests / 61 assertions); Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:216-219`
  - **Problem:** duration() calls $this->date_start->startOfDay() and $this->date_end->startOfDay() without ->copy(). The 'date_start'/'date_end' attributes use the default 'datetime' cast, which yields a MUTABLE Carbon instance that Eloquent caches in-memory for the life of the model. I verified empirically (in the project's own Carbon) that startOfDay() returns the same instance and mutates it to 00:00:00. So invoking duration() silently zeroes the time component on the reservation's own cached date_start/date_end for the rest of the request. The sibling trait HandlesAvailabilityDates::checkMinimumDate (line 48) is careful to do $date->copy()->startOfDay() for exactly this reason; this method is the inconsistent one. I confirmed there are NO callers of duration() anywhere in src/ or resources/ (it exists only for consumer templates via the resrv tag), so the bug is fully latent today and warrants low rather than medium.
  - **Fix:** Use copies: return (int) $this->date_start->copy()->startOfDay()->diffInDays($this->date_end->copy()->startOfDay(), true);
  - **Evidence:** Line 37-38 cast date_start/date_end to 'datetime' (mutable Carbon). Line 218: `return (int) $this->date_start->startOfDay()->diffInDays($this->date_end->startOfDay(), true);` — no copy(). Verified in repo: Carbon::parse('2026-06-01 14:30')->startOfDay() returns the SAME instance with time zeroed ('same instance: yes'). grep for '->duration()' across src/ and resources/ returned zero call-sites.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L12 — Unrestricted mass assignment ($guarded = []) on Reservation and ChildReservation**
  - **Fixed:** Replaced `$guarded = []` on both models with explicit `$fillable` allow-lists (derived from an authoritative `Schema::getColumnListing()` dump + a sweep of every writer) covering exactly the columns app code writes, while withholding the primary key `id` — so a future `fill()/update()` with untrusted input can't reassign the PK (cross-record clobber) or set any unknown/future column. **Independent-review note — the report's own `$guarded` suggestion was unsafe:** I verified the writers and the creates *mass-assign* `status`, `price`, `payment`, `payment_id` (HandlesReservationQueries) and the Checkout steps mass-assign `total`/`payment_surcharge`/`payment_gateway`/`customer_id`, so the report's proposed `$guarded = ['id','status','price','payment','total','payment_id','payment_gateway']` would have **silently dropped those on create/update and broken reservation creation**. The first `$fillable` option was therefore the only safe one. Confirmed not exploitable today (no `update($request->all())`/`fill($input)` anywhere). **Honest scope:** the financial/status columns stay fillable because the creates legitimately mass-assign them — fully protecting them would require refactoring every writer to `forceCreate`/`forceFill`, disproportionate for a non-exploitable low gap; this change is defense-in-depth (PK + unknown/future-column protection + an explicit, auditable writable surface), not airtight money-field protection. Status changes still flow only through `transitionTo()` (direct assignment). **Caught mid-fix:** my first cut also withheld `created_at`/`updated_at`, which silently broke the time-simulation tests (`ReservationAbandonedTest` sets `updated_at`, `ExpireReservationsTest` sets `created_at`); since those are legitimately set and timestamp-forgery is low-impact, I kept the timestamps fillable and withhold only `id`. **Tests:** added `test_reservation_does_not_mass_assign_guarded_columns` (a `fill(['id'=>…,'status'=>…])` leaves `id` untouched but applies `status`) — has teeth (pre-fix `id` was assignable). Re-ran every writer-exercising suite post-fix: Mail+Jobs+Reservation (119) and Payment+Availability+Console+Checkout+AvailabilityMultiResults+CheckoutForm (265) — **384 tests green**; Pint clean.
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:34`
  - **Problem:** Reservation (line 34) and ChildReservation (line 17) both use protected $guarded = [], so every column — status, type, price, payment, total, payment_id, payment_gateway, reference — is mass-assignable. I confirmed it is NOT currently exploitable: all create()/update() call sites pass server-computed arrays with explicit keys (HandlesReservationQueries, Checkout, controllers), and I found no ->update($request->all()) / ->fill($input) anywhere in src/. So this is purely a defense-in-depth gap, not a present vulnerability — the original 'medium' overstates it; low is appropriate. Adding it would harden a money-handling model against a future accidental fill($input).
  - **Fix:** Switch to an explicit $fillable allow-list of columns written by app code, or at minimum $guarded = ['id','status','price','payment','total','payment_id','payment_gateway']; keep status transitions exclusively through transitionTo().
  - **Evidence:** Reservation.php:34 `protected $guarded = [];`, ChildReservation.php:17 same. All writers use explicit arrays (e.g. HandlesReservationQueries.php:77-92). grep for `update($request`, `fill($request`, `create($request->all` in src/ returned no matches — not exploitable today.
  - _security · partially-confirmed · high confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-security sweep(s)_

- [x] **L13 — PriceClass cast's get() is shadowed by explicit getXAttribute accessors**
  - **Fixed:** Documented the intentional dual mechanism instead of collapsing it — the finding's premise is partly wrong and its proposed "pick one mechanism" fix is unsafe. **Independent-review correction:** `PriceClass::get()` is **not** dead. The accessor only wins on *direct* access (`$reservation->price` → Price object, for money math); on array/JSON serialization Laravel routes class-castable keys back through the cast (`mutateAttributeForArray` → `getClassCastableAttributeValue`), so `$reservation->toArray()['price']` is the cast's *formatted string*. That string is load-bearing: `ResrvCheckoutRedirect` plus the gateway `handleRedirectBack()`/`toArray()` payloads expose it to Antlers templates on the payment-complete page. Both report-suggested fixes (make `get()` return a Price object, or drop the cast) would flip serialization to a Price object and break that template/payload contract — and making the *shared* cast return an object would additionally enable Laravel's object-cache for a **mutable** Price (`multiply()`/`add()`/`subtract()` mutate in place), risking cross-read corruption across the 7 models that use the cast. For a low-severity maintainability nit, collapsing the mechanisms is disproportionate and risky, so the proposed fix must **NOT** be applied. Instead: added concise comments at the `$casts` block and above the money accessors in `Reservation.php` explaining why both halves exist and must stay in sync, and locked the contract with `ReservationPriceCastTest` (asserts price/payment/payment_surcharge/total are Price objects on direct access **and** formatted strings via `toArray()`). No runtime change. Pint clean; `tests/Reservation` + `PriceTest` green (121 tests, 347 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:36-44,83-101`
  - **Problem:** price/payment/payment_surcharge/total are declared BOTH in $casts as PriceClass::class (lines 39-42) AND have explicit accessors getPriceAttribute/getPaymentAttribute/getTotalAttribute/getPaymentSurchargeAttribute (lines 83-101). In Laravel the explicit getXAttribute accessor wins on read, returning a Price OBJECT — tests rely on this (e.g. RateIndependentSharedTest.php:229 $row->price->format(), FixedPricingCpTest.php:170). That means PriceClass::get() (Price.php:107-112, which returns a formatted STRING) is effectively dead for these attributes; only PriceClass::set() is exercised on write (no setXAttribute mutators exist). Having both a cast and an accessor for the same attribute is a maintenance trap: read vs write behavior can silently diverge if one is changed without the other. Low severity.
  - **Fix:** Pick one mechanism. Preferably keep the cast and make Price::get() return the Price object (matching the accessors), then delete the four redundant getXAttribute methods; or drop the cast entries for these columns and keep accessors plus an explicit setter.
  - **Evidence:** Casts lines 39-42 map price/payment/payment_surcharge/total to PriceClass. Accessors 83-101 return Price::create($value) (a Price object).
