Price::get (Price.php:107-112) returns ->format() (string). Tests use ->price->format() (object API). No setXAttribute methods present, so cast set() handles writes.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L14 — entry() and getEntryAttribute() return inconsistently shaped 'deleted entry' payloads**
  - **Fixed:** The substantive defect was **already resolved** by the H14 commit + the `entryToArray()`/`ResolvesReservationEntries` refactor (verified by independent review): `emptyEntry()` now returns `['id','title','slug','url']` (null url) — the **same key set** as the live augmented array, no more `api_url`/`permalink` divergence — and `getEntryAttribute()`, `ReservationResource`, `ReservationCalendarResource` and `Report` all resolve through the shared `entryToArray()` helper. `Index.vue:95` now reads `entry?.url` (not `permalink`), so a live entry renders a link and a deleted entry (`url: null`) renders plain text — the intended behavior. This is locked by existing tests `ReservationCpTest::test_index_payload_exposes_entry_url_for_the_listing_link` and `::test_index_payload_renders_deleted_entry_as_plain_text` (assert `url` present / `permalink` absent for both live and deleted). This iteration closed the only residual — the finding's "share one resolver" maintainability ask: `serializeReservation()` (the `show()` path) was still re-hardcoding `toAugmentedArray(['id','title','slug','url'])`, so it now delegates to `$reservation->entryToArray($entry)`, leaving the key set in exactly one place (`entryToArray()`, mirrored by `emptyEntry()` with a pointer comment). `entry()` intentionally stays separate — it returns a live Entry **object** because the payment gateways call `entry()->collection->handle()` — with `emptyEntry()` as its shared fallback. Behaviour-identical; Pint clean; `tests/Reservation` green (106 tests, 315 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:53-56,143-148,615-623`
  - **Problem:** Two near-duplicate entry resolvers exist with inconsistent fallback shapes. getEntryAttribute() (143-148) returns toAugmentedArray(['id','title','slug','url']) for a live entry, else emptyEntry(). emptyEntry() (615-623) returns ['id','title','api_url','permalink']. I confirmed Statamic's toAugmentedArray($keys) returns exactly the requested keys, so the live shape is [id,title,slug,url] (NO permalink) and the deleted shape is [id,title,api_url,permalink] (NO slug/url). The inconsistency is real, but the reviewer's note about which keys consumers read is partly off: the actual CP list (Index.vue:95-96) reads reservation.entry?.permalink and .title — which means a LIVE entry (no permalink key) renders with no link, while a DELETED entry (permalink='#') renders a link to '#': the inverse of intended behavior. Calendar reads entry['title'] (present in both, fine). show()/serializeReservation uses entry() and passes the augmented array [id,title,slug,url]; Show.vue only reads entry?.title. So the divergent shapes mainly surface as a broken/incorrect permalink link in the list. Low severity (UI link defect plus maintainability).
  - **Fix:** Have entry() and getEntryAttribute() share one private resolver, and make emptyEntry() return the SAME key set the live augmented array uses. Align that key set with what the Vue pages actually read (add 'permalink'/'url' consistently) so live vs deleted shapes are identical and the Index.vue link works for live entries.
  - **Evidence:** getEntryAttribute (143-148): toAugmentedArray(['id','title','slug','url']) else emptyEntry(). emptyEntry (615-623): ['id','title','api_url','permalink']. Verified Entry::toAugmentedArray($keys) returns only requested keys (HasAugmentedInstance.php:33 -> toAugmentedCollection($keys)->all()). Index.vue:95 `v-if="reservation.entry?.permalink"` :href=entry.permalink — permalink absent from live augmented shape but present (='#') in emptyEntry.
  - _maintainability · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

### Availability & Rates

- [x] **L15 — Duplicate same-rate/same-date cart selections bypass server-side price validation**
  - **Fixed:** Independent review confirmed the pre-flight gap (the aggregation collapses each rate+date group to `$group->first()`'s price, so a duplicate selection with a tampered lower price slipped past `confirmAvailabilityAndPrice`) **and** confirmed it is not exploitable for money loss — `Reservation::validateTotal()` recomputes every child price via `getPricing()` for PARENT reservations and throws `ReservationDriftException` before any payment, so a tampered child only produces an orphan PENDING row, never an underpayment. **Chose a minimal hardening over the proposed fix:** recomputing each price via `Availability::getPricing()` inside `createMultiReservation()` would add N pricing queries on the hot creation path and triplicate work the pre-flight + drift check already do. Instead, since identical rate+dates always resolve to the same per-unit price, the aggregation now rejects any group whose members carry **divergent** prices (zero extra queries, 6 lines). Combined with the existing `confirmAvailabilityAndPrice` (which already catches a *uniformly* tampered group against the server price), the pre-flight now fully validates duplicate-selection prices. **Test:** added `AvailabilityMultiResultsTest::test_duplicate_same_rate_date_selections_with_divergent_prices_are_rejected` — verified it FAILS pre-fix (tampered cart is accepted, "Component has no errors", parent reservation created) and PASSES post-fix (rejected at pre-flight with an `availability` error, `assertDatabaseMissing` confirms no row). Pint clean; full `tests/Livewire` suite green (294 tests, 936 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:161-195`
  - **Problem:** The aggregation logic gap is real: validateMultiAvailabilityAndPrice() groups selections by rate_id|date_start|date_end, takes $group->first() for the price, and only validates that first member's price (x total quantity). A second selection in the same group with a tampered low price is never price-checked here, and createMultiReservation() (HandlesReservationQueries.php:109-149) writes each un-aggregated $selection['price'] to its child and sums them into the parent. $selections is public and NOT #[Locked], so a crafted Livewire request can tamper it. HOWEVER this is NOT exploitable for money loss: the checkout flow re-validates server-side. Checkout::handleFirstStep() -> confirmReservationIsValid() -> Reservation::validateReservation() -> validateTotal() recomputes EVERY child price from scratch via Availability::getPricing() for PARENT reservations (Reservation.php:344-376) and compares the recomputed $dbTotal against the stored parent total ($frontendTotal from reservation->price in HandlesPricing::calculateReservationTotals line 19). A tampered child price makes the stored total differ from the recomputed one, throwing ReservationDriftException before any payment is initialized. So the real issue is a defense-in-depth weakness in the pre-flight check, not a money hole. Severity recalibrated from high to low.
  - **Fix:** Tighten the pre-flight check so it does not collapse distinct prices: validate each individual selection's price (not the group's first) before/while aggregating, e.g. recompute each selection's price server-side via Availability::getPricing in createMultiReservation() rather than trusting $selection['price'], and only use aggregation for the availability/quantity check.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 163-167: `$first = $group->first(); return array_merge($first, ['quantity' => $group->sum('quantity')]);` then line 171 `$perUnitPrice = $selection['price'];` validates only the first. createMultiReservation HandlesReservationQueries.php:115 `$childPrices[$index] = $selection['price']`. BUT Reservation.php validateTotal 346-372 for PARENT recomputes child prices via getPricing and `if (! $dbTotal->equals($frontendTotal)) throw new ReservationDriftException`. confirmReservationIsValid (Checkout.php:496-512) runs before payment; calculateReservationTotals (HandlesPricing.php:19) sets total from reservation->price.
  - _security · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L16 — Two incompatible getAvailability() contracts share one name across trait and components**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed the collision and mapped every caller: the trait helper `getAvailability(Collection $data, …): array` is used by `ResrvSearch.php:27`, `HandlesAvailabilityHooks.php:25` **and** `AvailabilityCollection.php:180` (a component that does *not* override it), while `AvailabilityResults` and `AvailabilityMultiResults` each redeclare `getAvailability(): void`, silently shadowing the trait method in those two components. Renamed the **component** lifecycle methods to `loadAvailability(): void` (declaration + the single internal `$this->getAvailability()` call in each) rather than the trait helper, because (a) the trait method genuinely *returns* availability so `getAvailability` is the accurate name and it has the most callers, and (b) the component method returns `void` and mutates `$this->availability`, so `load*` fixes a get-returns-void misnomer at the same time. Verified the component method is **not** frontend-wired (the `getAvailability()` references in `resources/js/fieldtypes/Availability.vue` are an unrelated local Vue function) and no test invokes it directly. Pure 4-site rename, no behaviour change; the footgun (a future component calling the 2-arg helper would hit the no-arg override) is gone. Pint clean; existing tests cover it — `AvailabilityResultsTest` + `AvailabilityMultiResultsTest` + `AvailabilityCollectionTest` green (134 tests, 429 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:28-45`
  - **Problem:** HandlesAvailabilityQueries declares `public function getAvailability(Collection $data, EntryCollection|LengthAwarePaginator|null $entries = null): array` (line 28), used by ResrvSearch scope (Scopes/ResrvSearch.php:27) and HandlesAvailabilityHooks (Traits/HandlesAvailabilityHooks.php:25). AvailabilityResults (line 117) and AvailabilityMultiResults (line 152) both redeclare `public function getAvailability(): void` with a completely different signature/purpose, silently overriding the trait method in those components. Not a bug today because the two consumers of the trait's 2-arg version (ResrvSearch, the hooks trait) do NOT override it and the components never need the trait's version. But it is a genuine footgun: a future refactor reusing the trait's getAvailability() from a component would silently hit the no-arg void override. Confirmed at low severity.
  - **Fix:** Rename one method to disambiguate, e.g. the component lifecycle method to loadAvailability()/refreshAvailability(), or the trait helper to getAvailabilityForSearch(), so the reusable query helper and the component lifecycle method are clearly distinct.
  - **Evidence:** Trait line 28: `public function getAvailability(Collection $data, EntryCollection|LengthAwarePaginator|null $entries = null): array`. AvailabilityResults.php:117 and AvailabilityMultiResults.php:152: `public function getAvailability(): void`. Trait-signature consumers: ResrvSearch.php:27 `$this->getAvailability($searchData)` and HandlesAvailabilityHooks.php:25 `$instance->getAvailability($searchData, $entries)`; neither class overrides it (HandlesAvailabilityHooks is only used by providers, not the components).
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L17 — Rate sorting by price uses float casting (SORT_NUMERIC) instead of integer-cents**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed both sites — `getAvailabilityCollection()` (now line 354) and `getMultipleRatesAvailability()` (now line 490) sorted `populateAvailability()` results (Collections whose `price` is a formatted decimal **string** via `->format()`) with `->sortBy('price', SORT_NUMERIC)`, which float-casts those strings. Replaced both with the decimal-safe pattern already used by the calendar/date-list sorts (`(int) …->raw()`) and `getCheapestRateAvailability` (`Price::create(...)->lessThan(...)`): `->sortBy(fn ($row) => (int) Price::create($row->get('price'))->raw())` (the `Price` facade is already imported). No behaviour change for distinct prices — every existing `RateSortingTest` outcome (cheapest wins, order tie-break, sold-out skip) still holds — but it removes the float comparison on money, matching the project's money-handling rule. No new test added: a float-vs-cents distinguishing case for 2-decimal prices would be contrived/brittle, and the sort behaviour is already comprehensively covered. Pint clean; `tests/Rate` + `tests/Availability` green (241 tests, 601 assertions; `RateSortingTest` 9/9).
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Availability.php:329, 444`
  - **Problem:** getAvailabilityCollection() (line 329) and getMultipleRatesAvailability() (line 444) both sort with `->sortBy('price', SORT_NUMERIC)`. 'price' is the formatted decimal STRING produced by populateAvailability() (line 506: `'price' => $prices['reservationPrice']->format()`), so SORT_NUMERIC casts those strings to PHP floats for comparison. This is inconsistent with the decimal-safe approach used elsewhere in the same file: getCheapestRateAvailability() (lines 457-464) compares via Price::create(...)->lessThan(...) on integer cents — and its own comment (lines 454-456) explicitly states it does so 'rather than float casts to stay decimal-safe' — while the calendar/date-list paths sort on `(int) $row->price->raw()` (lines 731, 843). For ordinary distinct prices float ordering is reliable, so impact is genuinely low; it is a latent consistency wart that contradicts the project's money-handling rule. Confirmed at low severity.
  - **Fix:** Sort using integer cents to match the rest of the file, e.g. `->sortBy(fn ($row) => (int) Price::create($row->get('price'))->raw())`. Price is already imported (use Reach\StatamicResrv\Facades\Price).
  - **Evidence:** Availability.php:329 `return $processed->sortBy('price', SORT_NUMERIC);`; :444 `$this->buildRatesAvailabilityCollection($entry)->sortBy('price', SORT_NUMERIC)`; :506 `'price' => $prices['reservationPrice']->format()` (a string). Contrast :463 `Price::create($rate->get('price'))->lessThan(...)`, :731 `->sortBy(fn ($row) => (int) $row->price->raw())`, :843 `->sortBy(fn ($items) => (int) $items->first()->price->raw())`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L18 — Calendar map can emit null entries for fully-booked dates**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed — `getAvailabilityCalendar()`'s query (now Availability.php:755-760) has no `available > 0` predicate, so for a date where every grouped row is sold out, `->firstWhere('available', '>', 0)` returns `null` and `->toArray()` keeps `['Y-m-d' => null]` mixed in with row arrays. Appended `->filter()` after the map (one line) so sold-out dates drop out entirely. Chose `->filter()` over normalizing to an explicit `['available' => 0]` shape because it is the smaller change **and** it unifies a sold-out date with a no-availability-row date — which is *already* absent from the map — so the frontend's existing "absent ⇒ not bookable" handling covers both, with no new third state. **Test:** added `RateAvailabilityTest::test_calendar_omits_fully_booked_dates_instead_of_emitting_null` — verified it FAILS pre-fix (the sold-out date key is present with a `null` value) and PASSES post-fix (key absent, available date still present). Pint clean; `tests/Rate` + `AvailabilitySearchTest` green (229 tests, 596 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Availability.php:729-732`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed. The query at lines 679-685 selects rows filtered only by `date >= today` (and optional rate), with NO `available > 0` predicate. The final map (line 731) is `->map(fn ($item) => $item->sortBy(...)->firstWhere('available', '>', 0))`. For any date where every grouped row has available <= 0, firstWhere() returns null, so the resulting array contains `['Y-m-d' => null]`. The output feeds the frontend Livewire AvailabilitySearch::availabilityCalendar() (src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:360-370) -> Vue calendar, mixing null with row arrays. Note the frontend Livewire flow is marked out-of-scope for the v6 upgrade per CLAUDE.md/TASKS.md, and no existing test asserts the sold-out shape, so this is a pre-existing inconsistent-contract issue rather than a v6 regression. Severity low.
  - **Fix:** Append `->filter()` after the map so sold-out dates are simply absent from the array, OR normalize them to an explicit `['available' => 0, ...]` shape. The filter approach is the smaller change and matches the implicit 'only available dates' contract.
  - **Evidence:** Availability.php:679-685 query has no `available > 0` filter (only `->where('date','>=', now()->startOfDay()...)`). Line 731 `->map(fn ($item) => $item->sortBy(...)->firstWhere('available', '>', 0))` — firstWhere returns null when no row matches, then `->toArray()` at line 732 keeps the null value keyed by date.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L19 — Rate::calculatePrice flat 'decrease' modifier can produce negative day prices**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed in both `calculatePrice()` and `calculateTotalPrice()` — the decrease branches (`->subtract($modifier)` / `->decreasePercent($amount)`) have no zero floor, so a misconfigured relative rate (flat decrease > base, or percent ≥ 100) yields a negative per-day price that flows into reservation totals and the calendar. Added a `protected floorAtZero(PriceClass $price): PriceClass` helper (`$price->lessThan(Price::create(0)) ? Price::create(0) : $price`) and applied it to the final result of **both** methods (uniform flooring covers percent + flat decrease, and the negative-`modifier_amount` edge case too). **Chose calculation-time flooring over the save-time validation alternative** because a flat decrease is compared against a base that varies per date/entry and is unknown at save time — only flooring is a complete fix; capping percent at 100 would still leave the flat case open. **Tests:** added 3 to `RateCpTest` (percent decrease 150%, flat decrease 150 vs base 100, total flat decrease 60×2 vs total 100) — verified they FAIL pre-fix (`-50.00`, `-50.00`, `-20.00`) and PASS post-fix (`0.00`); existing increase / in-bounds-decrease tests are unaffected. Pint clean; `tests/Rate` + `tests/FixedPricing` green (220 tests, 530 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Rate.php:267-286`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed. For a relative rate with modifier_operation='decrease', calculatePrice() does `$price->subtract($modifier)` (line 285) with no zero floor; for percent modifiers, decreasePercent() with percent >= 100 drives the result to zero/negative (Price.php:68-74 multiplies by `(100 - percent)/100`). The per-day result is summed across days in getPrices() (HandlesPricing.php:56 transform then line 62 add) and surfaced as the reservation price and into populateAvailability()/calendar (Availability.php:691-697, 800-805, 899-901). A misconfigured relative rate therefore yields a negative reservation total, which the moneyphp-based Price arithmetic carries through silently (Money supports negative amounts). calculateTotalPrice() (lines 293-311) has the same unfloored subtract at line 311. Severity low because it requires a misconfigured rate (admin error), not attacker input.
  - **Fix:** Clamp the per-day relative result to a minimum of zero in calculatePrice()/calculateTotalPrice() (e.g. after computing $result, `return $result->lessThan(Price::create(0)) ? Price::create(0) : $result;`) and/or validate modifier_amount (<= base) and percent (0-100) when saving a Rate.
  - **Evidence:** Rate.php:281-285 `$modifier = Price::create($this->modifier_amount); return $this->modifier_operation === 'increase' ? $price->add($modifier) : $price->subtract($modifier);` — no floor. Price.php:68-70 decreasePercent `$by = bcmul(100 - $percent, 0.01, 4); $this->multiply($by);` — negative $by when percent>100. Consumed in getPrices via HandlesPricing.php:56 `$pricesCollection->transform(fn ($price) => $rate->calculatePrice($price))`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L20 — itemsExistAndHavePrices uses inclusive end date while the engine treats date_end as exclusive**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed the divergence — `itemsExistAndHavePrices()` uses inclusive `where('date','<=',$date_end)` + an inclusive `diffInDays(...->addDay())` count, whereas the booking-engine queries (`availableBetween`, `itemAvailableBetween`, `getLockedAvailabilities`) use exclusive `where('date','<',$date_end)`. Independent review showed this is actually a **consistent CP-vs-engine pattern**, not a stray bug: the inclusive methods are the CP/admin range operations (`itemsExistAndHavePrices` and `delete()` both use `<=`), driven by an admin typing a date range they mean inclusively, while the engine queries treat `date_end` as the exclusive checkout/departure day. The sole caller, the `ResrvAvailabilityExists` CP validation rule, passes the full CP-typed range, so the behaviour is **correct** — the only risk is a future caller reusing the method with an engine-style exclusive range. Took the report's recommended approach (aligning to exclusive is risky without auditing the CP rule): added a docblock spelling out the INCLUSIVE contract and contrasting it with the exclusive engine convention, so the foot-gun is documented. Documentation-only — zero behaviour change, so no new test; Pint clean and `tests/Availability` green (40 tests, 123 assertions) as a sanity check.
  - **Where:** `src/Repositories/AvailabilityRepository.php:115-129`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed as a real semantic divergence, correctly scoped low. Every booking query in this repository uses exclusive end dates (`->where('date','<',$date_end)`: availableBetween line 77, itemAvailableBetween line 94, itemPricesBetween line 110, getLockedAvailabilities line 242; plus CarbonPeriod::EXCLUDE_END_DATE at lines 349/391). itemsExistAndHavePrices() instead uses `->where('date','<=',$date_end)` (line 119) and `$expectedDays = diffInDays($date_start, $date_end->addDay())` (line 126, inclusive count). Its sole caller is the ResrvAvailabilityExists CP validation rule (src/Rules/ResrvAvailabilityExists.php:27,37) where dates are treated inclusively (it validates the full range a CP user typed), so the behavior is internally consistent for that caller. The risk is purely a foot-gun: any future caller reusing this method with engine-style exclusive ranges gets an off-by-one. Documenting or aligning the contract is the right call.
  - **Fix:** Add a docblock to itemsExistAndHavePrices() explicitly stating it uses INCLUSIVE end-date semantics (CP rule contract), distinct from the exclusive convention used by every other method in this repository, so future callers don't mix them. Aligning to exclusive is risky without auditing the CP rule's expectations.
  - **Evidence:** itemsExistAndHavePrices line 119 `->where('date', '<=', $date_end)` and line 126 `$expectedDays = (int) Carbon::parse($date_start)->diffInDays(Carbon::parse($date_end)->addDay(), true)`. Compare availableBetween line 77 `->where('date', '<', $date_end)` and getLockedAvailabilities line 242 `->where('date', '<', $date_end)`. Only caller: ResrvAvailabilityExists.php:27 and 37.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L21 — Capacity checks build per-day PHP loops over the full overlapping reservation set**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed — `validateMaxAvailableForDateRange` re-ran `$allOverlapping->filter(...)->sum('quantity')` for every requested day (O(days × overlapping)), inside the checkout `lockForUpdate` transaction, while `getExhaustedDatesForRates` already used a one-pass map. Replaced the per-day filter with a single-pass `$bookedPerDay` map (each overlapping reservation expanded once via `CarbonPeriod … EXCLUDE_END_DATE`), then an O(1) lookup per requested day — shrinking the work and the lock-held window for long stays / large overlapping sets. **Behaviour-preserving:** the map keys a reservation onto exactly `[date_start, date_end)` (date_end exclusive), which equals the original filter's `date_start.toDateString() <= D < date_end.toDateString()` condition; I bound the period with `->toDateString()` so a stray time component can't shift day boundaries. **Test:** added `RateSharedAvailabilityTest::test_max_available_is_enforced_per_day_for_partially_overlapping_reservations` (a booking spanning a day exhausted by *partially*-overlapping reservations is still rejected) to lock the per-day granularity the refactor must keep — passes both pre- and post-refactor. Pint clean; full `tests/Rate` green (206 tests, 485 assertions; `RateSharedAvailabilityTest` 37/37).
  - **Where:** `src/Repositories/AvailabilityRepository.php:339-360, 391-403`
  - **Problem:** validateMaxAvailableForDateRange (391-403) iterates CarbonPeriod over the requested range and, for EACH day, re-runs $allOverlapping->filter(...)->sum('quantity') — O(days × overlapping). getExhaustedDatesForRates (339-360) already uses the better one-pass approach (build a date=>quantity map by expanding each reservation once). validateMaxAvailableForDateRange runs inside the checkout lockForUpdate transaction (useLocks=true), so the redundant per-day filtering also extends the lock-held window. Confirmed; low (only material for long stays / large overlapping sets, but the lock-window aspect makes it worth fixing).
  - **Fix:** In validateMaxAvailableForDateRange, build a date=>quantity map from $allOverlapping in a single pass (the exact dateCounts pattern already in getExhaustedDatesForRates, lines 346-353), then look up each requested day in O(1). This keeps the lock-held window minimal.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 393-397: `foreach ($period as $date) { ... $activeQuantity = $allOverlapping->filter(fn ($r) => ...)->sum('quantity'); ... }` — full-collection filter per day, with $useLocks=true applying lockForUpdate at lines 376/386. Lines 346-353 in getExhaustedDatesForRates build $dateCounts in one pass — the recommended pattern.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L22 — itemAvailableBetween INNER JOINs resrv_rates without filtering soft-deleted rates**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed the asymmetry — `itemAvailableBetween()` joins `resrv_rates` with no `deleted_at` guard, while `itemAvailableBetweenForAllRates()` and `applyPublishedRateFilter()` both exclude soft-deleted rates. Independent review pinpointed the gap to the **rate path**: `applyRateFilter()` only filters `rate_id`, and `resolveBaseRateId()` resolves via `Rate::withoutGlobalScopes()->find()` (so a soft-deleted rate still resolves), so without a guard the join surfaces a soft-deleted rate's rows; the no-rate path was already safe via `applyPublishedRateFilter()`'s `whereNull(deleted_at)` subquery. The live caller (`getSpecificItemCollection` resolves the rate with SoftDeletes-aware `Rate::find` and returns empty if gone) masks it end-to-end, so this is a defense-in-depth consistency gap, not an active bug. Added `->whereNull('resrv_rates.deleted_at')` (one line) to match the sibling and make the method safe in isolation. **Test:** added `RateAvailabilityTest::test_availability_query_excludes_soft_deleted_rate` — verified it FAILS pre-fix (1 row surfaced for a soft-deleted rate) and PASSES post-fix (0 rows). Pint clean; `tests/Rate` + `tests/Availability` green (247 tests, 609 assertions).
  - **Where:** `src/Repositories/AvailabilityRepository.php:85-101`
  - **Problem:** The asymmetry is real: itemAvailableBetween() joins resrv_rates with no `whereNull('resrv_rates.deleted_at')`, whereas itemAvailableBetweenForAllRates() (line 150) does add it and applyPublishedRateFilter() (line 59) checks deleted_at in its subquery. However the practical impact is smaller than 'medium' claims. The only caller, getResultsForItem() at Availability.php:160, is invoked from getSpecificItemCollection(), which when given an explicit rateId first resolves the rate via `$this->getRate()` (Rate::find(), respecting SoftDeletes) and returns empty if it is gone (lines 354-358). When no rateId is passed, the query still applies applyPublishedRateFilter() which DOES exclude deleted/unpublished rates via the whereExists subquery. So a soft-deleted rate cannot actually surface availability rows through the live caller. This is a defense-in-depth consistency gap in an isolated method, not an active correctness bug.
  - **Fix:** Add `->whereNull('resrv_rates.deleted_at')` to itemAvailableBetween() to match itemAvailableBetweenForAllRates() and remove the asymmetry, so the method is safe in isolation.
  - **Evidence:** itemAvailableBetween() at lines 91-100 joins resrv_rates with no deleted_at guard; itemAvailableBetweenForAllRates() line 150 has `->whereNull('resrv_rates.deleted_at')`. getSpecificItemCollection() (Availability.php:354-362) calls `$rate = $this->getRate()` (Rate::find, SoftDeletes-aware) and returns empty resource if `! $rate`, masking the gap. The no-rate path uses applyPublishedRateFilter() (line 97) which checks `whereNull('resrv_rates.deleted_at')` (line 59).
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L23 — Quantity has no lower-bound validation; negative/zero quantity inflates stock and bypasses caps**
  - **Fixed:** Independently confirmed the engine-internal weakness — `setQuantity()` only guarded the upper bound, so a negative quantity reached `addToPending()` as `available - $quantity` (inflating stock) and a quantity ≤ 1 skipped the `quantity > 1` price multiplier. Also confirmed the finding's own caveat: the two cited FormRequest classes are dead code (only self-referenced) and the live Livewire path (`AvailabilityData`) already enforces `int` + `min:1`, so this is defense-in-depth, not an exploitable hole. Fix is a one-guard symmetric mirror of the existing upper-bound check at the single chokepoint both the safe and "unsafe" engine paths funnel through: `if ($quantity < 1) { throw new AvailabilityException(__('You have to reserve at least one.')); }`. Left the dead request classes untouched (deleting public addon classes is out of scope for this finding and riskier than the benefit). **Test:** added `AvailabilityValidationTest` (zero + negative quantity both throw `AvailabilityException`) — verified it FAILS pre-fix and PASSES post-fix. Pint clean; `tests/Availability` + `tests/Rate` (251) and `tests/Livewire` + `tests/Extra` + `tests/Option` (335) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityDates.php:55-64`
  - **Problem:** setQuantity() genuinely lacks a lower bound — it only checks `$quantity > config('resrv-config.maximum_quantity')` and would accept 0/negative, which would flow into addToPending() as `available - $quantity` (increasing stock for negatives) and skip the `quantity > 1` price multiplier. So the engine-internal weakness is real. HOWEVER the reviewer's claimed exploit path is wrong: the two cited request classes (AvailabilityRequest, ReservationCreateRequest) are DEAD CODE — grep shows no controller or route references them, and no public HTTP controller feeds a user-supplied quantity into the availability engine. The ONLY public entry point is the Livewire frontend form src/Livewire/Forms/AvailabilityData.php, which types `public int $quantity = 1` and validates `'quantity' => ['sometimes','integer','min:1', new ResrvMaxQuantity]` (line 38). So crafted negative/zero quantities cannot actually reach the engine through any live path. This is a defense-in-depth hardening, not an exploitable high-severity hole.
  - **Fix:** Add a lower-bound guard in setQuantity(): `if ($quantity < 1) { throw new AvailabilityException(...); }`. Adding `min:1` to the two FormRequest classes is harmless but pointless since they are unused; consider deleting those dead request classes instead.
  - **Evidence:** HandlesAvailabilityDates.php:59 only checks the upper bound: `if ($quantity > config('resrv-config.maximum_quantity'))`. AvailabilityRepository.php:261 does `'available' => $availability->available - $quantity`. HandlesPricing.php:79 guards multiplication with `if ($this->quantity > 1 && ...)`. BUT grep for AvailabilityRequest/ReservationCreateRequest returns only their own files (no controller/route uses them), and AvailabilityData.php:38 enforces `'integer','min:1'` on the real frontend path with `public int $quantity = 1` at line 15.
  - _security · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

### Lifecycle (events / listeners / jobs)

- [x] **L24 — ExpireReservations declares ShouldQueue but relies on request session and is only ever dispatched sync**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed the footgun — the job `implements ShouldQueue` yet `handle()` reads `session('resrv_reservation')`, while **every** dispatch site is `dispatchSync()` (`Availability.php:83,93`, `HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:81`); a stray `dispatch()` would queue it onto a worker with no HTTP session, silently no-op'ing the session-expiry block. `SerializesModels`/`InteractsWithQueue`/`Queueable` were all dead weight (no constructor payload, never queued). Chose the minimal option matching actual usage: dropped `implements ShouldQueue` and the three unused queue traits/imports, keeping only `Dispatchable` (all `dispatchSync()` needs) — net removal of code, no behavior change. The session-into-constructor refactor was the more complex alternative and isn't warranted for a sync-only job. **Test:** added `ExpireReservationsTest::test_it_is_not_a_queued_job_because_it_depends_on_the_request_session` (asserts not `instanceof ShouldQueue`) — verified it FAILS pre-fix and PASSES post-fix. Pint clean; `tests/Jobs` + `tests/Availability` green (47 tests) and the `dispatchSync()` call sites still pass.
  - **Where:** `src/Jobs/ExpireReservations.php:15-29`
  - **Problem:** ExpireReservations implements ShouldQueue (line 15) yet handle() reads `session('resrv_reservation')` (line 27-28), and the only dispatch sites use dispatchSync() (Availability.php:72,82; HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:81). The ShouldQueue contract invites a plain dispatch(); if anyone ever queues it, it runs on a worker with no HTTP session, so the session-expiry block silently no-ops and behavior diverges from the sync path. SerializesModels (line 17) is dead weight since there is no constructor payload. This is a footgun, not a current bug.
  - **Fix:** Drop `implements ShouldQueue` (and the SerializesModels/InteractsWithQueue traits) if it must run synchronously; or refactor so the session-dependent expiry id is passed into the job constructor explicitly rather than read from the global session, making it queue-safe.
  - **Evidence:** `class ExpireReservations implements ShouldQueue { use Dispatchable, InteractsWithQueue, Queueable, SerializesModels;` with no constructor. handle(): `if (session()->has('resrv_reservation')) { ... session('resrv_reservation') ... }`. All dispatch sites are `ExpireReservations::dispatchSync();`.
  - _best-practice · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L25 — ExpireReservations unconditionally expires the current session's PENDING reservation on every availability search**
  - **Fixed (documented as intended; no functional change):** Independent review confirms the verifier's verdict — this is deliberate, safe behavior, not a bug. Verified the mechanics (the session block runs before the `minutes_to_hold` early-return and expires the session's PENDING hold regardless of the window) and the scoping: `ExpireReservations` is dispatched only from the 5 search/browse components (via `HandlesAvailabilityQueries`) and `Availability`'s search methods — never from the checkout step components (`Checkout`, `CheckoutForm`, `CheckoutPayment`, `Extras`, `Options`), so an actively-booking user is never killed mid-checkout. Expiring a PENDING (unpaid) hold on return-to-search simply releases stock back to search via `ReservationExpired → IncreaseAvailability` — no money or integrity impact. Gating it on `minutes_to_hold` would be a product decision, not a fix, so behavior is left unchanged. Applied the finding's only actionable suggestion: expanded the inline comment to record the design decision, and pinned the (previously untested) behavior with a regression test. **Test:** added `ExpireReservationsTest::test_expires_the_session_held_pending_reservation_on_search_even_within_the_hold_window` (a fresh session-held hold the time-window prune would keep is still expired, while an unrelated fresh hold is untouched) — verified it FAILS when the session block is disabled and PASSES with it. Pint clean; `tests/Jobs` green (6 tests).
  - **Where:** `src/Jobs/ExpireReservations.php:27-29`
  - **Problem:** The code does exactly what the finding describes: the session block (`if (session()->has('resrv_reservation')) { expireSafely(find(...)); }`) runs before the `minutes_to_hold == false` early return, and expire() expires any reservation whose status is still PENDING regardless of the hold window. BUT the framing as a premature/accidental bug is wrong — it is deliberate and well-scoped. The inline comment states the intent ('If a user already started a reservation that he didn't finish, expire it right away'), and the job is only triggered from availability SEARCH paths (Availability::getAvailable / getAvailabilityForEntry, used by AvailabilityResults / AvailabilityMultiResults). The checkout STEP components (Extras, Options, CheckoutForm, CheckoutPayment) do NOT call getAvailable/getAvailabilityForEntry, so an actively-booking user is never killed mid-checkout. The only way to hit it is to return to the search/results page — i.e. start a NEW search — at which point releasing the prior unfinished hold so its stock is searchable again is reasonable, intended behavior. So this is a design choice worth documenting, not a correctness bug.
  - **Fix:** No functional change required. If desired, add a code comment/docs note clarifying that returning to search intentionally abandons the in-progress hold, and confirm product intent. Only if the product wants in-window holds preserved across re-search should the session expiry be gated on the same minutes_to_hold window used in getReservation() (HandlesReservationQueries.php:57-64).
  - **Evidence:** Lines 27-29 run before line 30's `if (config('resrv-config.minutes_to_hold', false) == false) return;`. Comment line 26: 'If a user already started a reservation that he didn't finish, expire it right away.' grep confirms getAvailable/getAvailabilityForEntry are only called from AvailabilityResults/AvailabilityMultiResults search flows, not from the checkout step components.
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L26 — ProcessDataImport leaves cache entry on failure and store() only checks cache presence (re-dispatch ambiguity)**
  - **Fixed:** Independently confirmed — `handle()` forgot the cache key only on success (so a mid-loop throw left it), there was no `failed()` hook (hard failures were silent), and the trailing `return true;` contradicted the `@return void` docblock. Applied the proportionate subset for a Low/best-practice finding: removed the dead `return true;` and added a `failed(\Throwable $exception)` handler that clears the cache key and `Log::error`s the failure — the idiomatic Laravel mechanism, which directly addresses the title (no lingering entry blocks re-upload, and the failure is surfaced). **Deliberately skipped** the over-engineered suggestions: `$tries`/retries is a queue-config/behavior change out of scope here; a dispatch-lock in `store()` is unnecessary because the upserts are idempotent (a double-submit is safe) and the cache key is already per-user scoped (`importCacheKey()`); CSV deletion was left out because the file is per-user and overwritten each import (bounded), `DataImport::$path` is private with no accessor (cleanup would add API surface + file-deletion risk), and `index()` already `Cache::forget`s on revisit. **Test:** added `ProcessDataImportTest::test_failed_clears_the_cache_key` — verified it FAILS without the cleanup (cache lingers) and PASSES with it. Pint clean; `tests/DataImport` green (26 tests).
  - **Where:** `src/Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:30-146`
  - **Problem:** `handle()` only forgets the cache key on full success (Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:143). If the job throws mid-loop the cache entry remains; upserts are idempotent so a retry is safe, but the controller's `store()` guard is just `Cache::has('resrv-data-import')` (DataImportCpController.php:64) with no de-dup, so a double-submit dispatches the same job twice. The job declares no `$tries`/`failed()` (class lines 19-21), so a transient failure is dropped with no admin feedback while the cache entry and CSV file linger. The trailing `return true;` (line 145) in a `@return void` job (declared line 28) is dead code.
  - **Fix:** Forget the cache key (and delete the uploaded CSV) in a try/finally or a `failed()` handler, add `public $tries`, surface failures, and make store() idempotent (e.g. a dispatch lock). Remove the dead `return true;`.
  - **Evidence:** Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:143 `Cache::forget('resrv-data-import');` only after the full `each` completes; line 145 `return true;` in a method documented `@return void` (line 28). No `$tries`/`failed()` in the class. DataImportCpController.php:64 `if (! Cache::has('resrv-data-import'))` is the only store() guard, line 68 `ProcessDataImport::dispatch();`.
  - _best-practice · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L27 — DecreaseAvailability/IncreaseAvailability re-query childs() instead of using the loaded relation**
  - **Fixed:** Confirmed both `decreaseMultiple()` (`DecreaseAvailability:30`) and `incrementMultiple()` (`IncreaseAvailability:29`) used `$event->reservation->childs()->get()` (the relation builder = a fresh query) instead of the `childs` property (lazy-loaded once, reused if already loaded). Verified the change is safe in every dispatch path: children are created exactly once, atomically, in the parent-creation transaction (`HandlesReservationQueries:150`) *before* `ReservationCreated` fires, and are never mutated afterward (every other `ChildReservation::` reference is a read query), so a cached relation can never be stale; in the create flow the parent instance hasn't accessed `childs`, so the property lazy-loads fresh — identical to before, "at worst neutral" as the finding notes. Fix is the trivial 2-line swap to `$event->reservation->childs`. **Test:** `decreaseMultiple` was already covered (3 tests dispatch `ReservationCreated($parent)`), but the `incrementMultiple` (parent expire/cancel) path was untested — added `AvailabilityEventsTest::test_expiring_a_parent_reservation_restores_its_children_stock` (expire a parent, assert the child's stock is restored while an unrelated normal hold remains). Verified it FAILS when the listener doesn't load childs and PASSES with the fix. Pint clean; `tests/Availability` + `tests/Listeners` + `tests/Rate` green (256 tests).
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/DecreaseAvailability.php:30-31`
  - **Problem:** decreaseMultiple() (DecreaseAvailability line 30) and incrementMultiple() (IncreaseAvailability line 29) call $event->reservation->childs()->get() — the relation builder (fresh query) — rather than the $event->reservation->childs property. One extra query per stock adjustment on parent reservations. These listeners fire on every cart reservation create/expire/cancel/refund. Confirmed; genuinely low impact (a single extra query, not N+1) but trivially fixable.
  - **Fix:** Use the $event->reservation->childs property so an already-loaded collection is reused, or eager-load childs when the event is dispatched. Verify the parent is freshly persisted with childs available; if childs were never loaded, the property access still issues exactly one query (same as now), so this is at worst neutral.
  - **Evidence:** DecreaseAvailability.php line 30 `$childs = $event->reservation->childs()->get();`. IncreaseAvailability.php line 29 `$childs = $event->reservation->childs()->get();` — both use the childs() method (query builder) rather than the childs property.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L28 — EntryDeleted cleanup uses the localized id, so deleting a localization is a no-op and the listener is inconsistent with the rest of the codebase**
  - **Fixed (corrected approach — the report's proposed fix is harmful and was NOT applied):** Independent review confirms the no-op-on-localization observation but rejects the proposed "resolve the origin id, then delete" fix. That fix would make a single-localization delete run `Availability::where('statamic_id', <originId>)->delete()` and **wipe the surviving origin's availability** — directly violating the finding's own statement that "the origin data SHOULD survive a localization delete," and actively *reducing* robustness in the cited guard-bypass case (it would delete a still-booked origin's availability). I proved this: temporarily applying the proposed fix empties `resrv_availabilities` on a localization delete (test below fails, "table is empty"). The genuine consistency target is `Entry::syncToDatabase()` (the EntrySaved mirror), which **skips localizations** via `if ($entry->hasOrigin()) { return; }` and only writes for the origin. The correct symmetric fix for the delete side is the same skip — so only the origin's own deletion cleans up its shared, origin-keyed availability/pricing. Added that guard (mirroring `syncToDatabase`). This is provably **zero behavior change** for current data: single-site entries have no origin (guard not taken); multisite localization deletes already matched 0 origin-keyed rows. **Test:** added `MultisiteEntryDeletionTest::deleting_a_localization_keeps_the_origin_availability` — verified it PASSES with the guard and FAILS under the report's proposed fix (origin availability wiped). Pint clean; `tests/Multisite` + `tests/Availability/AvailabilityCpTest` (non-multisite cleanup path) + `tests/Listeners` green (43 tests). Note: this does not by itself fix the orphaned-localizations concern — that is H5's already-applied guard fix.
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/EntryDeleted.php:19-30`
  - **Problem:** EntryDeleted::handle() sets $id = $event->entry->id() (the localized id when a localization is deleted) and runs Availability::where('statamic_id', $id)->delete() plus the dynamic-pricing-assignments delete on that id. Because all availability/pricing is keyed by the ORIGIN id (confirmed by MultisiteAvailabilityTest::availability_is_stored_with_origin_entry_id), deleting a localization matches zero rows - it is a harmless no-op, NOT a leak (the finding's 'leak' framing is inverted: the origin data SHOULD survive a localization delete). The genuine issue is consistency: this listener resolves ids differently from the reservation/availability writers (which use getDefaultSiteEntry/origin). The real damage is the combination with finding #1: in the 'Delete' multisite flow the origin delete is correctly blocked by the guard, so the origin's availability survives, but its localizations were hard-deleted (per finding #1), leaving translations gone while origin+availability+reservations remain. Resolving the origin id here is still the right consistency fix, and it makes the listener robust if the guard ever lets a localization through.
  - **Fix:** Resolve the origin id first for consistency: $id = $event->entry->hasOrigin() ? $event->entry->origin()->id() : $event->entry->id(); before deleting availability and dynamic-pricing assignments. Note this alone does not fix the orphaned-localizations problem - finding #1's guard fix is the primary remedy.
  - **Evidence:** `$id = $event->entry->id();` then `Availability::where('statamic_id', $id)->delete();` (EntryDeleted.php:19-22) and the dynamic_pricing_assignments delete keyed on the same $id (lines 25-28). Availability is origin-keyed (MultisiteAvailabilityTest lines 166-177: localized id yields 0 availability rows). So on a localization delete the WHERE matches nothing.
  - _bug · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L29 — Detach-localizations flow can orphan reservations: detached locale becomes a standalone empty entry while the booked origin survives**
  - **Fixed (documented + safety-tested; block/migrate intentionally not implemented):** Independently confirmed the mechanics — `detachLocalizations()` (vendor) sets each localization's `origin(null)`, merges parent data, and `save()`s it; that `EntrySaved` reaches `AddResrvEntryToDatabase → Entry::syncToDatabase`, where `hasOrigin()` is now false so the early-return is bypassed and a fresh `resrv_entries` row is created with no availability. But the "orphan reservations" framing overstates the impact: the booked origin survives intact (its origin-keyed availability and reservations are untouched, and its own delete stays blocked by the guard), and reservations are **not** orphaned — they remain with the surviving origin. The detached entry simply starts empty, which is defensible for a "make independent" action. Per the finding's own scoping ("out of strict scope... at minimum document"), and weighing importance vs. complexity for a Low edge case, I did **not** add blocking (fragile — detach fires only a generic `EntrySaved`, no dedicated event; high false-positive risk distinguishing detach from normal saves) or reference-migration (a product-decision feature). Instead: documented the behavior with a concise comment at the exact spot in `Entry::syncToDatabase`, and pinned it with a characterization test. **Test:** added `MultisiteEntryDeletionTest::detaching_localizations_keeps_origin_data_and_leaves_the_detached_entry_without_availability` — asserts the origin's availability + pending reservation survive the detach (the key no-corruption safety property) and that the detached entry becomes its own `resrv_entries` row with no availability. Pint clean; `tests/Multisite` (14) + `tests/Availability/AvailabilityCpTest` (26) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/PreventEntryDeletionWithActiveReservations.php:12-27`
  - **Problem:** Statamic's multisite delete action also offers 'Detach' (DeleteMultisiteEntry::run with behavior === 'copy'), which calls $items->each->detachLocalizations(): each localization is save()d with origin set to null. That EntrySaved fires AddResrvEntryToDatabase -> Entry::syncToDatabase, and since the detached entry now has hasOrigin() === false, the early return at Entry.php:64 no longer applies and it is inserted into resrv_entries as a brand-new item with no availability and no reservations, while existing reservations still point at the old origin id. Detach happens BEFORE the origin delete in run() (line 54 then line 59), and the deletion guard only reasons about the origin id, so it neither anticipates nor blocks the detach path. The origin delete itself would still be blocked by the guard if reservations exist, but the localizations have already been turned into independent empty entries by then. Genuine edge case; low severity is correct.
  - **Fix:** Out of strict scope but worth handling: decide whether detaching localizations of a booked item should be blocked or should migrate availability/reservation references to the detached entries. At minimum document that detach does not migrate resrv data and leaves the detached locale as an empty (no-availability) entry.
  - **Evidence:** `if ($behavior === 'copy') { $items->each->detachLocalizations(); }` then later `$items->reject(fn ($entry) => $entry->delete())` (DeleteMultisiteEntry.php:53-59). detachLocalizations save()s each loc with `->origin(null)` (vendor Entry.php:303-314), firing EntrySaved -> AddResrvEntryToDatabase::handle -> syncToDatabase. Once origin is null, syncToDatabase's `if ($entry->hasOrigin()) return;` (Entry.php:64) is bypassed and a fresh resrv_entries row is created with no availability. The guard only checks the origin id (line 18) and is never consulted during detach (no EntryDeleting fires on a save).
  - _correctness · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L30 — Inconsistent delete semantics: Entry mirror is soft-deleted but its availability is hard-deleted, so a re-saved entry comes back with no availability**
  - **Fixed (documented the intentional asymmetry + characterization test; did NOT change the delete policy):** Independently confirmed the mechanics — `Entry` uses `SoftDeletes` (Entry.php:21) so `SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase` soft-deletes the mirror, while `Availability` has no `SoftDeletes` (Availability.php:27-29) so the sibling `EntryDeleted` listener hard-deletes availability + dynamic-pricing assignments; `syncToDatabase` then restores the trashed mirror on re-save (Entry.php:69,81-83) but availability stays gone. Both fixes the report proposes are wrong for this codebase: (a) `forceDelete` the mirror would break the **tested** restore behavior (`AvailabilityCpTest::test_entry_deletion_soft_deletes`, `ImportEntriesTest::test_import_entries_restores_soft_deleted_entries`) **and** orphan the `resrv_entry_extra` links keyed to `resrv_entries.id` on re-import — the soft-delete is deliberately load-bearing (preserves the mirror PK so per-entry extras/options config survives a delete→re-sync cycle); (b) making availability soft-deletable needs a migration **and** would not work consistently because `AvailabilityRepository`'s raw, driver-specific SQL bypasses Eloquent's soft-delete global scope — wildly disproportionate to a Low finding. The asymmetry is in fact a reasonable design (preserve per-entry *config*; wipe volatile *stock*) that was simply undocumented and so read as a bug. **Fix:** added a PHPDoc to `SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase::handle()` (+ `: void` return type) and a one-line note at the restore site in `Entry::syncToDatabase`, both stating that availability/dynamic-pricing are intentionally hard-deleted and NOT restored (a restored entry keeps its extras config but comes back with no stock). **Test:** added `AvailabilityCpTest::test_entry_deletion_hard_deletes_availability_which_a_mirror_restore_does_not_bring_back` pinning the contract — after delete the mirror is soft-deleted while availability is gone; after re-save the mirror is restored (single row, `deleted_at` null) but availability is still absent. Pint clean; `tests/Availability/AvailabilityCpTest` (27) + `tests/Console/ImportEntriesTest` + `tests/Listeners/PreventEntryDeletionWithActiveReservationsTest` + `tests/Multisite/MultisiteEntryDeletionTest` (39 total) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase.php:12`
  - **Problem:** On EntryDeleted, SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase does Entry::where('item_id', ...)->delete(), and the Entry model uses SoftDeletes (Entry.php:21) with a deleted_at column (create_resrv_entries migration line 25), so the mirror row is only soft-deleted. The sibling EntryDeleted listener HARD-deletes the availability rows (Availability does NOT use SoftDeletes - confirmed, class Availability has no `use SoftDeletes`) and hard-deletes dynamic-pricing assignments. syncToDatabase() restores a soft-deleted mirror on re-save (Entry.php:80-82 withTrashed + restore()), but the availability is permanently gone. So a delete-then-recreate cycle silently restores the entry mirror with zero stock/pricing. The mixed model creates a false impression that deletion is recoverable. Low/maintainability is correct.
  - **Fix:** Pick one policy. If recovery is the goal, make availability/dynamic-pricing soft-deletable too (or have the restore path warn that availability is not restored). If recovery is not a goal, hard-delete (forceDelete) the mirror row to match the availability cleanup.
  - **Evidence:** `Entry::where('item_id', $event->entry->id())->delete();` (line 12); `use ... SoftDeletes;` and `$table->softDeletes()` give a soft delete. EntryDeleted.php:22 `Availability::where('statamic_id', $id)->delete()` is a hard delete (Availability class has no SoftDeletes trait). Restore path: `if ($resrvEntry->trashed()) { $resrvEntry->restore(); }` (Entry.php:80-82).
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

### Pricing & Money

- [x] **L31 — DynamicPricingList filters deep watcher fires on programmatic resets despite the resetting guard timing**
  - **Fixed (documented the invariant; no behavioural change, as the finding itself concluded):** Independently re-read `DynamicPricingList.vue:236-297` and confirmed there is **no present bug** — the verifier's own conclusion ("No behavioural fix required"). `resetFilters()` sets `resetting=true`, clears search + the three filters synchronously, and flips the flag back + calls `applyFilters()` exactly once inside `nextTick`; both `watch(searchQuery)` and `watch(filters)` early-return while `resetting` is true. Because the flag is read at watcher-callback execution time and only reset after the watcher flush (guaranteed by nextTick), a reset triggers exactly one reload — no double-fire, no missed fire. The only suggested fixes were optional: a reactivity refactor (imperative change handlers, drop the watchers, re-implement the 300ms debounce) — meaningful new code + behavioural risk with no functional benefit and no JS test harness in this PHP addon (no vitest/jest) — or the documentation alternative the finding offers ("keep the early-return guard but document that resetting must remain true until after the flush"). Took the proportional path: added a one-line note on the `resetting` ref and a 3-line comment at `resetFilters()` making the flag/nextTick invariant explicit. **Test:** none — comment-only, behaviour-preserving change to a Vue component with no JS test infrastructure. Verified `npm run cp:build` compiles cleanly (235 modules); minified output is byte-identical (comments stripped), so no tracked dist artifacts changed.
  - **Where:** `resources/js/components/DynamicPricingList.vue:236-297`
  - **Problem:** resetFilters sets resetting=true, synchronously clears searchQuery and the three filters keys, then defers resetting=false + applyFilters() to nextTick (lines 285-297). Both watch(searchQuery) (lines 236-243) and watch(filters) (lines 245-249) early-return on resetting.value, so the resets do not double-fire applyFilters. This works correctly today because the resetting flag is read at the moment the watcher callback runs and is still true through the synchronous reset and the pre-flush watcher invocation; nextTick (where the flag flips back and applyFilters is called) runs after the DOM-update flush. The reviewer's claim of a flush-ordering dependency is somewhat overstated: a flag read inside the callback is robust to 'pre' vs 'post' flush as long as it is reset after the flush, which nextTick guarantees. The genuine fragility is the dual source of truth (searchQuery ref + filters reactive both driving applyFilters via separate watchers) plus reliance on the flag rather than imperative control — a maintainability nit, not a present bug.
  - **Fix:** Optional: consolidate search+filters into a single imperative applyFilters invoked from change handlers and drop the watcher-based reset guard, or keep the early-return guard but document that resetting must remain true until after the flush. No behavioural fix required.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 237 and 246 both start with `if (resetting.value) return;`. resetFilters lines 286-296 set resetting=true, clear values synchronously, then `nextTick(() => { resetting.value = false; applyFilters(); });`. The guard is a value read inside the callback, not a flush-order trick.
  - _Vue · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L32 — AddDynamicPricingsToReservation writes the coupon to session with the GETTER form — it is a silent no-op**
  - **Fixed (one-line getter→setter + regression test):** Independently confirmed — `session('resrv_coupon', $event->data->coupon)` (line 13) is Laravel's two-argument getter (reads `resrv_coupon`, returns the second arg as a default), so it never writes. The read site `DynamicPricing::couponNotApplied()` (DynamicPricing.php:402) keys coupon-gated dynamic pricing off `session('resrv_coupon')`, and the correct setter form is used elsewhere (Checkout.php:535 `session(['resrv_coupon' => ...])`). As the finding notes, shipped flows already seed the session (HandlesReservationQueries.php:100,162 pass `coupon: session('resrv_coupon')`), so today it's a latent no-op that only bites a programmatic caller constructing `ReservationData(coupon: ...)` without pre-seeding the session — but the fix is a single character-level change with zero added complexity, so clearly worth doing to make the listener self-sufficient. **Fix:** changed line 13 to the array (setter) form `session(['resrv_coupon' => $event->data->coupon]);`. **Test:** added `tests/Listeners/AddDynamicPricingsToReservationTest::test_reservation_created_persists_the_coupon_to_the_session` — dispatches `ReservationCreated` with `new ReservationData(coupon: 'TESTCOUPON')` and asserts `session('resrv_coupon')` holds it, after first asserting the session is empty so the listener's own write is isolated (exactly the latent path the bug breaks). Confirmed the test FAILS on the old getter form (`null` vs `'TESTCOUPON'`) and passes after the fix. Pint clean; `tests/Listeners/AddDynamicPricingsToReservationTest` + `tests/Availability/AvailabilityEventsTest` + `tests/DynamicPricing/DynamicPricingApplyTest` (41 total) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/AddDynamicPricingsToReservation.php:12-14`
  - **Problem:** `session('resrv_coupon', $event->data->coupon)` is Laravel's two-argument GETTER form: it READS key resrv_coupon and returns $event->data->coupon as the default; it writes nothing. To persist you must pass an array: `session(['resrv_coupon' => $event->data->coupon])`. DynamicPricing::couponNotApplied() reads `session('resrv_coupon')` (line 406) when deciding whether coupon-gated dynamic pricing applies. The core claim is correct. However the practical impact is lower than 'medium': the only in-repo callers that build ReservationData already source the coupon FROM the session — HandlesReservationQueries.php:96 and :157 both pass `coupon: session('resrv_coupon')`, and the normal Checkout flow writes the key at Checkout.php:533. So in every shipped path the value the listener tries to (fail to) write is already present in the session. The bug only bites a future/programmatic caller that constructs ReservationData(coupon: ...) without first seeding the session. So it is a latent no-op rather than an active failure today.
  - **Fix:** Change line 13 to `session(['resrv_coupon' => $event->data->coupon]);` so the listener becomes self-sufficient regardless of caller.
  - **Evidence:** Line 13: `session('resrv_coupon', $event->data->coupon);` (getter+default). Compare the correct setter at Checkout.php:533: `session(['resrv_coupon' => $data['coupon']]);`. Callers HandlesReservationQueries.php:96,157 pass `coupon: session('resrv_coupon')`, so the session already holds the value in shipped flows.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L33 — Price::create(null) for missing original_price triggers a deprecation and is dead-coded with `?? null`**
  - **Fixed (null guard + dropped dead `?? null`; deprecation premise was already resolved by H7):** Independent review found the finding's **primary premise is now stale** — the H7 fix already replaced `new Money(bcmul($price, 100), ...)` with `DecimalMoneyParser` in `Price::create()` (Price.php:20-37), so the `bcmul(null, 100)` deprecation/PHP-9 TypeError no longer exists. Regression-checked instead.
