- [x] **L88 — File input is uncontrolled and not reset after submit/failed validation**  _(closed without code change — independent review found the finding invalid for this architecture. (1) The "not reset on success" half is moot: `DataImportCpController::confirm()` responds with `Inertia::render('resrv::DataImport/Confirm')` — a different page component — for BOTH the happy path and CSV-content errors, so `Index.vue` unmounts entirely and the form/input cease to exist; the proposed `onSuccess: () => { form.reset('file'); fileInputRef.value.value = '' }` would target a component mid-teardown — dead code by construction. Returning to the page is always a fresh GET → `index()` → clean remount (which also `Cache::forget`s the stale import). (2) The "stale file on validation failure" half describes correct, desirable UX, not a bug: on an Inertia back-redirect the same component re-renders with state preserved, and the input's filename and `form.file` remain CONSISTENT — `form.file`'s only write path is the input's own `@change`, and nothing ever clears the input programmatically, so the claimed "re-selected but submitted the old one" desync has no reachable path. Retaining the file while the user fixes a collection/delimiter error spares a re-pick; clearing it (the `onError` variant) would be strictly worse. Blast radius was already nil per the report's own note: the actual import runs from the server-stored per-user CSV. Importance ≈ 0 vs. net-new permanently-dead lifecycle code — hard fail of the proportionality gate, so the correct fix is none. No code touched → Pint/PHPUnit n/a.)_
  - **Where:** `resources/js/pages/DataImport/Index.vue:23-25, 17-21`
  - **Problem:** Real but minor, and partly inherent to the web platform. setFile (Index.vue:23-25) stores event.target.files[0] into form.file; the native <input type="file"> (line 70) cannot be value-bound from JS for security reasons, so 'binding the input to form' as the finding suggests is not actually possible - that part of the description is slightly wrong. The valid points: form.post(props.confirmUrl, { forceFormData: true }) (lines 17-21) has no onSuccess/onError/onFinish, so on a validation failure the page re-renders with form.errors while the native input still shows the prior filename and the stale File stays in form.file, and on success the form is not reset. This can produce 'I re-selected but it submitted the old one' confusion. Low severity - it does not corrupt data, just UX/memory hygiene. Note the confirm step also persists the uploaded CSV to cache via DataImport, so the actual import uses the server-stored file, not the in-memory File, limiting the blast radius.
  - **Fix:** Add lifecycle handling: form.post(url, { forceFormData: true, preserveScroll: true, onSuccess: () => { form.reset('file'); if (fileInputRef.value) fileInputRef.value.value = ''; } }). Use a ref on the <input> to clear it, since file inputs cannot be reset via v-model.
  - **Evidence:** Index.vue:23-25 `function setFile(event) { form.file = event.target.files[0] ?? null; }`. Lines 17-21 `form.post(props.confirmUrl, { forceFormData: true });` - no callbacks. Line 70 `<input id="file" name="file" type="file" ... @change="setFile" />` - not (and cannot be) value-bound.
  - _best-practice · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L89 — Store page reports 'Import finished!' before the queued import has run**  _(fixed with the report's primary suggestion: the one-line copy reword. Independent review confirmed the finding — `store()` dispatches `ProcessDataImport` (ShouldQueue) and immediately renders Store.vue's unconditional "Import finished!", so on redis/database/sqs drivers the admin sees success for a job that is merely enqueued, and both failure modes stay invisible (missing cache → `Log::warning` + return; exception → `failed()` logs only). One refinement to the report: on the `sync` driver the old copy was actually accurate (dispatch runs inline; an exception would 500 before the render), so the bug is driver-dependent. New copy "Import started! Availability will update in a few moments." is safe on BOTH drivers — "started" is never false since dispatch always precedes render, while "finished" was false exactly when it mattered. The alternatives were rejected on proportionality for a cosmetic Low: queue-driver-branched copy (+4 lines of controller logic/prop/ternary for marginal precision on sync installs) and real status feedback via completion flag + Inertia partial-reload polling (a small subsystem). No lang-file churn (short CP strings are their own translation keys per Statamic convention; "Import finished!" appears in no lang file); DataImportCpTest asserts status/cache behavior, not copy, so no test changes. Verified: `npm run cp:build` green; JS-only so Pint/PHPUnit n/a.)_
  - **Where:** `resources/js/pages/DataImport/Store.vue:21-24`
  - **Problem:** DataImportCpController::store() (src/Http/Controllers/DataImportCpController.php:62-73) calls ProcessDataImport::dispatch() and then immediately renders resrv::DataImport/Store, which statically shows __('Import finished!') (Store.vue:21-24). ProcessDataImport implements ShouldQueue (src/Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:19), so on any non-sync queue driver (redis/database/sqs) the job is merely enqueued, not run, when the admin sees 'Import finished!'. There is no progress or failure feedback. The job itself handles a missing cache entry by logging a warning and returning, so a silently-failed/not-yet-run import still shows success. Real impact is limited (the import is idempotent-ish and the message is cosmetic), hence low severity, but the copy is misleading on production queue drivers.
  - **Fix:** Reword the message to reflect async dispatch (e.g. 'Import started - availability will update shortly.'), or branch on the queue connection (sync vs non-sync) to choose copy. For real feedback, persist a completion/status flag (e.g. clear/poll the 'resrv-data-import' cache key) and reflect it on the page via Inertia partial reloads.
  - **Evidence:** Controller: `ProcessDataImport::dispatch(); return Inertia::render('resrv::DataImport/Store', ...)`. Job: `class ProcessDataImport implements ShouldQueue`. Store.vue: `{{ __('Import finished!') }}` rendered unconditionally.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

### Affiliate / Customer / Data / Misc

- [x] **L90 — updateStandardRate() unconditionally overwrites a customized 'default' rate title and double-processes per blueprint**  _(fixed per the report, both halves, ~12 lines in the command. Independent review confirmed: (1) `updateStandardRate()` selected by `slug='default'` only and force-wrote `title='Standard Rate'`, while the property-rate path guards with `->where('title', $slug)` — so a renamed default rate (or any re-run scenario without the guard) got clobbered; (2) the call sits inside the per-blueprint loop, so a collection with several property-less availability blueprints reprocessed and re-counted the same rate. Fix: added `->whereIn('title', ['default', 'Default'])` — verified every production creation path writes exactly 'Default' (data migration ×3 branches + `Rate::findOrCreateDefaultForEntry`), and the lowercase variant is kept because the existing test fixture's title=slug convention represents the same un-customized state at zero extra cost; plus a `$processedStandardRateCollections` dedupe array with early return. Note the dedupe's only observable effect is dry-run accuracy: in a real run the title guard already self-heals the second blueprint pass (title is no longer 'Default'), but dry-run makes no writes, so without dedupe it double-counts and reports a wrong projection — defeating dry-run's purpose. Added 2 tests: customized title survives the run; two property-less blueprints + dry-run still project exactly 1 update (helper split into `collectionWithAvailabilityField` + `availabilityBlueprint` to allow a second blueprint per collection). Verified: Pint clean; `tests/Console/UpgradeToRatesTest.php` 8/8 green incl. the pre-existing rename + idempotency tests. Follow-up from external review (valid, empirically reproduced): Artisan reuses command instances within one process, so the dedupe array recorded during a dry run leaked into a subsequent real run in the same process (Octane/deploy-script/`Artisan::call` sequences) and silently skipped the actual update — fixed by resetting per-run state (`$updatedCount` too, same pre-existing defect class) at the top of `handle()`; the reviewer's alternative of not marking during dry runs was rejected since it would reintroduce the dry-run double-count. Covered by `test_dry_run_followed_by_real_run_still_updates_the_default_rate` (fails without the reset); suite now 9/9.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Console/Commands/UpgradeToRates.php:139-171`
  - **Problem:** Two real inconsistencies, both verified. (1) Missing title guard: processCollection() guards the property-rate rewrite with `->where('slug', $slug)->where('title', $slug)` (lines 111-113) so it only touches un-migrated rates. updateStandardRate() selects only `->where('slug', 'default')` (lines 142-144) with NO title guard and blindly `$rate->update(['title' => 'Standard Rate'])` (line 164). An admin who renamed their default rate before running, or a second run, has the title forced to 'Standard Rate'. (2) Per-blueprint double processing: updateStandardRate($collection) is called inside `foreach ($collection->entryBlueprints() as $blueprint)` whenever a blueprint has no advanced_availability (lines 84, 97-101), so a collection with multiple property-less blueprints calls it once per blueprint — re-updating the same default rate and over-counting updatedCount. Real but low severity: this is a one-shot migration and at first-run time the default title is 'Default' (set in Rate::findOrCreateDefaultForEntry line 352), so the clobber mainly bites on re-runs or pre-renamed defaults.
  - **Fix:** Mirror processCollection(): guard the rewrite, e.g. `->whereIn('title', ['default','Default'])` (or `->where('title', 'default')`), so a customized title is left alone. De-duplicate per collection (track processed collection handles) so multiple property-less blueprints don't reprocess and double-count the same default rate.
  - **Evidence:** UpgradeToRates.php:111-113 (property rates) `->where('slug', $slug)->where('title', $slug)`; vs :141-144 (default rate) only `->where('slug', 'default')` then :164 `$rate->update(['title' => 'Standard Rate']);`. Call site :84 `foreach ($collection->entryBlueprints() as $blueprint)` and :97-100 `if (empty($propertyLabels)) { $this->updateStandardRate($collection); continue; }`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L91 — findAvailabilityField assumes every field config has a 'type' key**  _(fixed, one line. Independent review confirmed the finding and sharpened it: a field config without 'type' is legal in Statamic (hand-edited YAML; `Field::type()` itself defaults to `'text'`, so the framework explicitly tolerates the absence and renders a text field), and the failure mode is worse than the report's "undefined-array-key warning" — Laravel's `HandleExceptions` bootstrapper converts the E_WARNING into a thrown `ErrorException`, empirically reproduced via a new test (`ErrorException: Undefined array key "type"` from HandleExceptions.php:258). One such field would break every helper consumer for that blueprint: `EntryDeleted`/`PreventEntryDeletionWithActiveReservations` listeners, `ResrvHelper::collectionsWithResrv`, `UpgradeToRates`, `ImportEntries`. Fix deviates slightly from the report's `($field->config()['type'] ?? null)` in favor of `$field->type() === self::FIELD_TYPE` — Statamic's canonical accessor reads the same `$this->config` via `Arr::get(..., 'text')`, identical match semantics here (missing → 'text' → no match → continue), and strictly less code; trivially proportionate for a Low. Grep confirmed this helper is the only place in src/ doing the type comparison, so the fix surface is complete. Added `test_handles_fields_without_a_type_key_in_their_config` to the existing `tests/Unit/AvailabilityFieldHelperTest.php` (untyped field ordered before the availability field so the loop hits it); failed with ErrorException before the fix, green after. Verified: Pint clean; tests/Unit 69/69; tests/Listeners 5/5.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Helpers/AvailabilityFieldHelper.php:76-85`
  - **Problem:** Confirmed as a minor defensive-coding gap. findAvailabilityField() (line 79) does `if ($field->config()['type'] === self::FIELD_TYPE)` with direct array access. In practice Statamic Field configs essentially always carry a 'type' key, so this almost never triggers; but a malformed/edge-case config without 'type' raises an undefined-array-key warning. This runs over every field of every saved blueprint via the BlueprintSaved listener (ClearAvailabilityFieldCache) and the cached getHandle/getField/blueprintHasAvailabilityField lookups. Low severity — null-coalescing is a cheap correctness/robustness improvement.
  - **Fix:** Use null-safe access: `if (($field->config()['type'] ?? null) === self::FIELD_TYPE)`.
  - **Evidence:** AvailabilityFieldHelper.php:78-82 `foreach ($blueprint->fields()->all() as $field) { if ($field->config()['type'] === self::FIELD_TYPE) { return $field; } }` — direct ['type'] access with no isset/?? guard.
  - _best-practice · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L92 — DataImport.prepare() materializes the entire CSV into memory and the job has no chunking/batching**  _(closed without code change — independent review found half the finding already fixed and the other half mis-sized + disproportionate. (1) The robustness half ("no `$tries`/`backoff`/`failed()`") is STALE: `failed()` exists at ProcessDataImport.php:185-192 (added under [x] L26: logs the error, clears the cache key) plus `deleteImportFile()` (added under [x] L46), and `$tries` was deliberately rejected in L26's adjudication as a queue-config/behavior change — worker-level `--tries` governs, and retries already work when configured because intermediate attempts keep the cache (`handle()` clears it only on success; only final failure reaches `failed()`) and upserts are idempotent. Worse, L92's specific suggestion — a `failed()` that "preserves the cache entry for retry" — is wrong by construction: `failed()` runs only after ALL attempts are exhausted, so preserving the cache there enables no retry; it would just leave the stale entry that wedges the next import — i.e., re-introduce the exact bug L26 fixed. (2) The memory half is technically true (the `reduce()` accumulator — `mapWithKeys/reject` in the report's evidence is itself stale, replaced under M32 — holds all prepared row data) but the report's sizing "entries x 365 days" conflates two structures: the CSV format is one row per entry(/rate) with one COLUMN per date range, so `prepare()`'s output is O(rows × price-columns) small arrays (single-digit MBs for realistic imports); the ×365 per-day expansion happens in `handle()` per price-range item (`$dataToAdd`), which is already scoped per item and freed after each upsert — i.e., the big structures are already streamed at the granularity that matters, and "flush every N rows" is already the de-facto behavior the report itself concedes ("already loosely chunked"). A true streaming refactor would change `prepare()`'s keyed-by-id return shape, which is BOTH a pinned test contract (DataImportTest::test_prepare_aggregates_multiple_rows_for_the_same_entry — the M32 fix — asserts `->get($entryId)` merged counts) and a user-visible Confirm-page contract (`prepare(true)->all()` keyed by id; `take(1)` = first ENTRY with merged rows, not first CSV row), plus re-plumbing the job's per-entry `$defaultRateId` memo — a contract-changing refactor of code hardened across M32/M33/L26/L46 for an unquantified, near-zero win on a low-frequency admin tool the report itself rates "not a hot-path perf issue" at partially-confirmed confidence. Hard fail of the proportionality gate (precedent: L88), so the correct fix is none. No code touched → Pint/PHPUnit n/a.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Helpers/DataImport.php:55-87`
  - **Problem:** `SimpleExcelReader::getRows()` returns a streaming LazyCollection, but `prepare()` calls `->mapWithKeys(...)->reject(...)` (lines 55-81) which materializes all rows into an in-memory Collection. ProcessDataImport::handle then iterates it and builds per-period `$dataToAdd` arrays (Jobs/ProcessDataImport.php:38-141), and there is no `$tries`/`backoff`/`failed()` on the queued job. For large imports (entries x 365 days) this is a large in-memory structure with no streaming/chunked upserts. Real but low severity: this is a low-frequency admin batch tool, upserts are per-entry-row (already loosely chunked by the inner foreach over the period), and PHP/MySQL handle moderate sizes fine. The lack of `$tries`/`failed()` is a robustness gap, not a hot-path perf issue.
  - **Fix:** Stream the LazyCollection and flush upserts every N rows instead of materializing all rows; add `public $tries` and a `failed()` handler that logs and preserves the cache entry for retry.
  - **Evidence:** DataImport.php:55-81 `$reader->getRows()->mapWithKeys(...)->reject(...)` collapses the lazy stream. ProcessDataImport.php class (lines 19-21) declares no `$tries`/`failed()`. Inner loops build `$dataToAdd` arrays per entry before `Availability::upsert` (lines 119-138).
  - _performance · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L93 — DataImport reads the availability column positionally as the column after each price column**  _(fixed per the report's prescription — date-range pairing — plus the validation needed to make it fail loudly. Independent review confirmed both failure modes: (1) silent corruption — a numeric column between the pair (the natural place an admin puts `rate_id`) is read as `available`, passes the job's `is_numeric` validation, and overwrites real availability; empirically proven by a new test that read `available='10'` (the rate_id) instead of `'5'` pre-fix; (2) crash — a price column in last position indexes past `array_keys($row)` → E_WARNING → Laravel ErrorException (per L91's proof). The positional read survives unchanged from the original 2022 commit (212214b). The pairing information has always been in the headers — every fixture since 2022 uses `price:A|B,availability:A|B`, the resrv.dev docs don't document the format at all (checked: no data-import page exists), and M33 already established that price headers MUST carry date ranges — so matching by range uses the format's own contract. Fix in `prepare()`: per-row `$availabilityByRange` map (availability headers keyed by their `getDatesFromHeader` range, inheriting its trim/whitespace tolerance) replaces the positional read; `?? null` fallback flows into the job's existing skip-with-warning validation as defense in depth. Fix in `headersHaveCorrectFormat()`: every price header must have an availability header with the same range, with a specific error naming the offending header — surfaced at the confirm step (controller gates `prepare()`/`store()` behind `checkForErrors()`), consistent with M33's precedent. Deliberate behavior change, documented: a bare `availability` header (no date range) adjacent to its price column previously worked positionally and now errors at confirm — same adjudicated direction as M33 (bare `price` outlawed), trading an undocumented fragile layout for an explicit early error in a corruption-prone tool. Proportionality: ~+20 lines src (mostly restructuring inside existing loops), 2 tests; justified for a confirmed high-confidence silent-data-corruption bug. Existing fixtures unaffected (all properly paired; the bare-header fixture in `test_check_for_errors_rejects_a_price_header_without_a_date_range` already asserts errors). Verified: Pint clean; tests/DataImport 31/31 (29 pre-existing + 2 new, both red pre-fix).)_
  - **Where:** `src/Helpers/DataImport.php:63-78`
  - **Problem:** `available` is read with `$row[array_keys($row)[$index + 1]]` (DataImport.php:70), blindly assuming the availability value sits in the column immediately to the right of each `price` column. If columns are in a different order, an extra column is inserted, `rate_id` is placed between price and availability, or a price column is last, this reads the wrong cell — or an out-of-range index (PHP undefined-index warning, null availability) when a price column is the final column. The pairing is implicit and unvalidated. Severity low because the documented/expected CSV layout pairs them adjacently, but the lack of validation makes a slightly off layout corrupt data silently.
  - **Fix:** Match availability columns by their own `availability:date1|date2` header and pair to the corresponding price header by date range, rather than relying on positional adjacency.
  - **Evidence:** DataImport.php:64 `foreach ($row as $header => $value)`, line 65 `if (strpos($header, 'price') !== false)`, line 70 `$arrayToPush['available'] = $row[array_keys($row)[$index + 1]];` — positional next-column read with no bounds check.
  - _bug · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L94 — Affiliate cookie value is unsigned and missing explicit SameSite/Secure/HttpOnly intent**  _(closed with a documentation comment only — independent review found all three fix items either already true or counterproductive. (1) "Set explicit flags (httpOnly true, secure when https, sameSite lax)": already the EFFECTIVE behavior — `$next($request)->cookie(...)` routes through `ResponseTrait::cookie()` → the `cookie()` helper → `CookieJar::make()`, whose signature defaults `httpOnly=true`, and whose `getPathAndDomain()` injects the jar defaults that `CookieServiceProvider` wires from the host app's session config (`session.secure`, `session.same_site` — Laravel stock = 'lax', `session.path`/`domain`) — verified in vendor (CookieServiceProvider.php register(), CookieJar.php make()). Hardcoding flags in the addon would be a regression vector, not hardening: it would override deliberate site-level policy (notably `same_site=none` for iframe-embedded booking flows — a realistic deployment for a reservation addon) and forced `secure=true` breaks plain-HTTP local dev; Laravel's idiom centralizes cookie policy in session config precisely so packages don't fight it. (2) "Confirm resrv_afid is encrypted / not in EncryptCookies' except": the `$except` list belongs to the HOST APP (an addon cannot police it; default = all cookies encrypted; the middleware runs in `statamic.web` alongside `web`'s EncryptCookies, write/read symmetric). More fundamentally the threat model gives signing/encryption ZERO security delta: the value is the affiliate code, which any visitor sets through the front door via `?afid=CODE`; tampering grants nothing the legitimate flow doesn't — garbage codes resolve to null and every read re-resolves server-side (`Affiliate::published()->where('code', ...)` in HandlesAffiliates:11), and even the `allow_skipping_payment` escalation is reachable identically via the legitimate link, as the report itself concedes ("attacker can only self-attribute to a code they already know... re-resolved server-side") at self-rated LOW confidence. (3) "Combine with the published re-validation from finding #7": already done under [x] M34 on both set and read paths, with tests (AffiliateFrontTest covers set/skip/overwrite/unpublished-gating both ways). Behavioral fix surface = nil; the proportionate action taken is a 3-line comment in the middleware encoding the deliberate flag-inheritance decision (matching the codebase's decision-comment idiom) so a future contributor doesn't "harden" it into the override regression. Verified: Pint clean; tests/Affiliate 25/25.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Http/Middleware/SetResrvAffiliateCookie.php:25-28`
  - **Problem:** The cookie is set with `->cookie('resrv_afid', $afid, $affiliate->cookie_duration * 24 * 60)` (line 28), leaving secure/httpOnly/sameSite at framework defaults. Tamper-resistance depends entirely on `resrv_afid` being covered by Laravel's EncryptCookies middleware, which the addon does not ensure. The stored value is just the affiliate `code`, later trusted to attribute fees and (with allow_skipping_payment) to skip payment. Impact is limited — an attacker can only self-attribute to a code they already know, and the affiliate is re-resolved server-side at attribution — so low severity. Still worth explicit handling given it gates payment skipping. Compounds with finding #7 (no `published` check).
  - **Fix:** Set the cookie with explicit flags (httpOnly true, secure when https, sameSite 'lax'), confirm `resrv_afid` is encrypted (not in EncryptCookies' except list), and combine with the `published` re-validation from finding #7.
  - **Evidence:** SetResrvAffiliateCookie.php:28 `return $next($request)->cookie('resrv_afid', $afid, $affiliate->cookie_duration * 24 * 60);` — only name/value/minutes args; no path/domain/secure/httpOnly/sameSite. The value `$afid` is the raw affiliate code from the query string.
  - _security · confirmed · low confidence · also independently flagged by: xc-security sweep(s)_

- [x] **L95 — SetResrvSearchByVariables middleware is unregistered dead code and would write unvalidated input to session / throw on bad dates**  _(fixed via the report's first option — removal — extended to the middleware's whole dead plumbing chain. The latent bugs are real as described: present-but-malformed `date_start` + `duration` → unguarded `Carbon::parse` → 500, and arbitrary query strings persisted verbatim into `session('resrv_search')` (M36 hardened the read side and explicitly deferred the write side). Between the report's two options, register+harden was rejected as the riskier path: it would activate 4-years-dormant code on every `statamic.web` GET (interference surface with the modern Livewire search flow, which persists under separate `resrv_search:`-prefixed keys) AND need net-new validation code; removal has zero out-of-box behavior change (the chain never ran) and lands on the v6 major-version boundary, the canonical moment for dropping dead public classes.   - **Where:** `src/Http/Middleware/SetResrvSearchByVariables.php:20-36`
  - **Problem:** `SetResrvSearchByVariables` is not referenced anywhere outside its own class file — `ResrvProvider::$middlewareGroups` registers only `SetResrvAffiliateCookie`, and no route attaches it.   - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L96 — Report sums/averages money by coercing formatted decimal strings to float**
  - **Fixed:** `sumConfirmedReservations`/`avgConfirmedReservations` were already converted to the Price API during the M35/L97 work (reduce with `Price::add`, `divide` on the Price). Remaining site fixed here: `topSellerItems` per-item revenue now reduces in integer minor units via `Price::add` (clone before `divide` — Price mutates in place), with a single terminal `(float)` cast of the formatted result. The cast is deliberate: applying the report's "format once" suggestion verbatim (strings in the payload) would silently break the revenue column sort in `ReportsItemsTable.vue`, which only number-sorts `typeof === 'number'` values — and fixing that would mean a Vue change + `npm run cp:build` + dist churn, disproportionate for a Low. A single shortest-round-trip conversion of the final value cannot accumulate error. Tests: per-item exact-money assertions (3 × 10.01 → 30.03/10.01) added to `test_sum_and_avg_confirmed_reservations_return_exact_money`; `assertSame` float-type pins added to the consistency test so a future switch to strings trips loudly.
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Report.php:33-62`
  - **Problem:** `sumConfirmedReservations`/`avgConfirmedReservations` (lines 35/42) and per-item revenue in `topSellerItems` (lines 55-60) call `$reservation->price->format()` inside Collection `sum()`/`avg()`. `Price::format()` returns a decimal string (Money/Price.php:99-105, via DecimalMoneyFormatter), so the Collection coerces strings to float and adds with floating-point arithmetic — the exact float-money path the project's Price abstraction exists to avoid (CLAUDE.md). For reporting this is usually tolerable, but accumulated float error across many rows plus `round(..., 2)` (lines 55-60) can shift the last cents.
  - **Fix:** Aggregate via the Price API — reduce with `Price::add` over Price objects, or sum the integer `->raw()` cents and format once — instead of summing formatted decimal strings as floats.
  - **Evidence:** Report.php:35-37 `return $reservation->price->format();` inside `->sum(...)`; lines 42-44 inside `->avg(...)`; lines 55-60 same inside `round(...->sum(...))`. Money/Price.php:99-105 `format()` returns `(new DecimalMoneyFormatter(...))->format($this->money)` — a string.
  - _best-practice · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L97 — Report mixes confirmed-only occurrences with confirmed+partner revenue** _(already resolved by the M35 rewrite: `getTopItems()` and its confirmed-only filter were deleted; `topSellerItems()` now groups the constructor-loaded `$this->reservations` (confirmed+partner), so occurrences, revenue, avg and percentage all share one population — `getTopExtras()` likewise filters on `$this->reservations->pluck('id')`. Verified no `where('status', 'confirmed')` remains in Report.php. Regression-covered by `test_top_seller_items_counts_confirmed_and_partner_consistently`, which mixes partner reservations and asserts count=4 / percentage=4∕6 — values the old mixed-population code cannot produce. No code change needed.)_
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Report.php:47-95`
  - **Problem:** The constructor query (Report.php:24) selects `whereIn('status', ['confirmed', 'partner'])` into `$this->reservations`, which is used for per-item revenue/avg in `topSellerItems` (lines 55-60) and for the extras query (`getTopExtras`, line 102). But `getTopItems` (line 90) filters `where('status', 'confirmed')` only — excluding partner. So an item's `reservations` occurrence count (confirmed-only, from getTopItems) and its `total_revenue`/`avg_revenue`/`percentage` (computed from `$this->reservations`, confirmed+partner) are derived from inconsistent populations whenever partner reservations exist, producing mismatched per-item figures. Also note `percentage` (line 61) divides confirmed-only occurrences by `countConfirmedReservations()` which counts confirmed+partner — another mismatch.
  - **Fix:** Make `getTopItems` use the same status set as the constructor (`whereIn('status', ['confirmed', 'partner'])`) so occurrences and revenue share one population, or explicitly document the intended difference.
  - **Evidence:** Report.php:24 `->whereIn('status', ['confirmed', 'partner'])`. Report.php:90 `->where('status', 'confirmed')` in getTopItems. Lines 55-60 compute revenue from `$this->reservations->where('item_id', ...)` (confirmed+partner). Line 61 `round($item->occurrences / $this->countConfirmedReservations(), 2)` mixes the two.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

### Mail / Support / Providers

- [x] **L98 — FiltersByDate uses a date-truncated Carbon for >/< comparisons against a datetime column**
  - **Fixed:** Applied the proposed one-liner — the `</>` branch now uses `whereDate` like the `between` branch, so all three operators share date-only semantics matching the day picker. Note the finding under-scoped the impact: `date_start` is a **datetime** column too (`$table->datetime('date_start')`, time-enabled bookings carry real times), so `ReservationStartingDate` had the same After-boundary bug, not just `created_at` — same fix covers both. Only `>` (After) changes behavior; `< midnight` was already equivalent to `whereDate <`. Tests: new `tests/Reservation/ReservationDateFilterTest.php` (After/Before for `created_at`, After for time-enabled `date_start`) — verified the two After tests fail against the unfixed trait. Full Reservation suite green (121 tests).
  - **Where:** `src/Filters/FiltersByDate.php:59-65`
  - **Problem:** For </> the trait does `$query->where(self::$handle, $operator, Carbon::parse($values['value']['date']))` (line 65), where the parsed value is midnight 00:00:00, while the 'between' branch uses whereDate() (lines 53-54). ReservationMadeDate uses $handle='created_at' (a full datetime), so 'After 2024-01-01' becomes created_at > '2024-01-01 00:00:00', matching rows created later on Jan 1 itself — inconsistent with the date-only semantics of the between branch and the date picker UI. ReservationStartingDate uses $handle='date_start' (a DATE column, no time) so the inconsistency is harmless there. Confirmed; the finding is correctly scoped to the created_at (datetime) case. Low severity (day-boundary surprise on an admin filter).
  - **Fix:** Use whereDate for the </> branch too so all comparisons operate on the date portion: `$query->whereDate(self::$handle, $operator, $value);` at line 65.
  - **Evidence:** FiltersByDate.php lines 63-65: `$value = Carbon::parse($values['value']['date']); $query->where(self::$handle, $operator, $value);` vs the between branch lines 53-54 `$query->whereDate(self::$handle, '>=', ...)`. ReservationMadeDate.php: `protected static $handle = 'created_at';`. ReservationStartingDate.php line 11: `protected static $handle = 'date_start';` (DATE column, unaffected).
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L99 — Entry filter eager-loads all reservation item_ids and referenced entries in its constructor**
  - **Fixed:** As proposed — constructor deleted; option list now built in a memoized `entries()` helper (`??=`, so the empty-collection case still memoizes) called only by `fieldItems()` and `badge()`, and the PHP-side `pluck('item_id')->unique()` replaced with SQL `distinct()->pluck(...)`. Verified the mechanism first: `ScopeRepository::find()`/`all()` do `app($class)` per call, so every filtered data fetch re-ran both constructor queries just to call `apply()`, which never reads the list. Net ~+4 lines. Tests: new `tests/Reservation/ReservationEntryFilterTest.php` — options built from distinct reservation entries, and a query-log assertion that construct+apply runs zero SQL (verified it fails against the old eager constructor). ReservationCpTest (filters end-to-end) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Filters/ReservationEntry.php:15-24`
  - **Problem:** The constructor runs Reservation::pluck('item_id')->unique()->toArray() (full item_id column load) then Entry::query()->whereIn('id', $ids)->get() to build checkbox options. Because the constructor does this work, the queries execute every time the filter is instantiated — both when Scope::filters('resrv', []) lists filters for the index page (indexCp) and when QueriesFilters::queryFilters() calls Scope::find('reservation_entry') for an active filter on every data fetch. Confirmed as described; low severity (admin-only, bounded by distinct entries but the pluck materializes the whole column).
  - **Fix:** Use a single distinct query for item_ids: Reservation::query()->distinct()->pluck('item_id'), and lazily build $this->entries (e.g. memoize / build inside fieldItems() and badge() rather than the constructor) so the entry list is only computed when actually needed.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 17-23: constructor does `$ids = Reservation::pluck('item_id')->unique()->toArray();` then `$this->entries = Entry::query()->whereIn('id', $ids)->get()->flatMap(...)`. Statamic's QueriesFilters trait calls `Scope::find($handle, $context)` (constructing the filter) for every active filter, and ReservationCpController::indexCp line 39 constructs all filters via Scope::filters('resrv', []).
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [x] **L100 — Filters call count() on possibly-null values (TypeError risk in PHP 8)**
  - **Fixed:** Applied the proposed guards verbatim at all three sites — `empty($values['entry'])` / `empty($values['status'])` in the two `apply()` methods (also silences the undefined-key case, since `empty()` is warning-free) and `$values['status'] ?? []` in `ReservationStatus::badge()` (an empty badge string is then dropped by `queryFilters`' `reject(empty)`). Reachability re-verified independently: `index(FilteredRequest)` → `queryFilters($query, $request->filters)` passes the decoded, UI-controlled JSON values raw into `apply()`/`badge()`, so `{"reservation_status":{"status":null}}` 500s — but only behind CP auth + `use resrv`, confirming Low/robustness. Tests: null + missing-key no-op coverage for both filters and the badge (`ReservationEntryFilterTest`, new `ReservationStatusFilterTest`) — running them against the unfixed code reproduces exactly the three predicted TypeErrors. ReservationCpTest (autoApply path) green.
  - **Where:** `src/Filters/ReservationEntry.php:43`
  - **Problem:** ReservationEntry::apply() does `if (count($values['entry']) === 0)`; ReservationStatus::apply() does `if (count($values['status']) === 0)`; ReservationStatus::badge() does `array_map('ucwords', $values['status'])`. In PHP 8 count(null) and array_map over null are fatal TypeErrors. Statamic's QueriesFilters::queryFilters() calls apply()/badge() with whatever values the request sends for that filter handle, so a request that includes the filter handle with entry/status null (e.g. all checkboxes cleared but the filter still submitted) would fatal. This is a real defensive-coding gap. Correcting scope/severity: it is NOT reachable on normal listing render (apply/badge only run when the handle is present in $request->filters), and ReservationStatus is shielded by autoApply() returning ['confirmed','partner'] for the default case; ReservationEntry has no autoApply default but is also only applied when explicitly submitted. Realistic exploitability is low — hence low/nit, not a high-confidence crash on every page.
  - **Fix:** Guard with empty()/null-coalescing: in apply() use `if (empty($values['entry'])) { return; }` and `if (empty($values['status'])) { return; }`; in badge() use `array_map('ucwords', $values['status'] ?? [])` (or `collect($values['entry'] ?? [])`).
  - **Evidence:** ReservationEntry.php line 43: `if (count($values['entry']) === 0) {`. ReservationStatus.php line 41: `if (count($values['status']) === 0) {` and line 49: `return implode(', ', array_map('ucwords', $values['status']));`. QueriesFilters.php passes `$filter->values` (request-supplied) directly to apply()/badge() only for handles present in the filters payload.
  - _bug · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [x] **L101 — Year filter loads every reservation's date_start into PHP to build the dropdown**
  - **Fixed:** As proposed — distinct years now computed in SQL via a small driver `match` (`strftime('%Y', ...)` SQLite / `EXTRACT(YEAR ...)::int` Postgres / `YEAR(...)` MySQL-MariaDB), `DISTINCT ... ORDER BY year DESC`, values normalized to strings for option parity with the old `format('Y')` output. Driver branching is the documented house idiom (CLAUDE.md JSON-column guidance, AvailabilityRepository's `string_agg`/`group_concat`) since no portable year-extraction syntax exists (`SUBSTR` fails on PG timestamps without a cast). Unused `Carbon` import dropped; `apply()`'s `whereYear` untouched (already portable). Tests: new `tests/Reservation/ReservationYearFilterTest.php` (distinct+desc options, apply-by-year) kept free of driver-specific SQL assertions so the pgsql suite can run them — verified green on BOTH sqlite and `phpunit.pgsql.xml`, and failing against the old PHP-side implementation.
  - **Where:** `src/Filters/ReservationStartingDateYear.php:18-30`
  - **Problem:** fieldItems() runs Reservation::pluck('date_start')->map(fn => Carbon::parse(...)->format('Y'))->unique() — it materializes the date_start column of every reservation row and parses each value in PHP just to compute the distinct list of years for a <select>. This runs whenever Scope::filters('resrv', []) is called to render the listing page (ReservationCpController::indexCp line 39 instantiates all filters and calls fieldItems()). The reviewer's mechanism is accurate. I downgrade severity from medium to low: this is a CP admin-only listing (low traffic, authenticated 'use resrv' users), not a public hot path, and Carbon parsing of a date column is cheap per row. It is still unnecessary full-column work that scales linearly with the table.
  - **Fix:** Compute distinct years in SQL, e.g. Reservation::query()->selectRaw('DISTINCT EXTRACT(YEAR FROM date_start) AS y')->orderByDesc('y')->pluck('y') (MySQL/Postgres differ on the year function; use a DB-portable expression or distinct()->reorder()->pluck on a year expression) so only the handful of distinct years are returned.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 20-22: `$years = Reservation::pluck('date_start')->map(function ($date) { return Carbon::parse($date)->format('Y'); })->unique()->toArray();`. ReservationCpController.php line 39: `'filters' => Scope::filters('resrv', []),` triggers fieldItems() on every index page render.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **L102 — ResrvMinimumDuration reads $value['date_start']/['date_end'] without guarding for missing keys**
  - **Where:** `src/Rules/ResrvMinimumDuration.php:17-27`
  - **Problem:** The rule is attached to the dates array in AvailabilityData::rules() as ['required', 'array', new ResrvMinimumDuration] (no 'bail'), so Laravel still invokes the custom rule even when 'dates' fails 'required'/'array'. The component's initial state is `public array $dates = [];` (empty). When dates is [] or lacks the keys, Carbon::parse($value['date_start']) raises an 'Undefined array key' E_WARNING and parses null as now(); both dates become now() so duration is 0. With the default minimum_reservation_period_in_days = 1 (config/config.php line 36), the < minimum branch fires, surfacing a spurious 'period is smaller than the minimum' error stacked on top of the real 'required' error, plus PHP warnings. Confirmed; low severity (UX/noise, not a crash).
  - **Fix:** Early-return when the keys are absent at the top of validate(): `if (! isset($value['date_start'], $value['date_end'])) { return; }` before computing the duration.
  - **Evidence:** ResrvMinimumDuration.php line 19: `$duration = (int) Carbon::parse($value['date_start'])->startOfDay()->diffInDays(Carbon::parse($value['date_end'])->startOfDay(), true);` with no key guard. AvailabilityData.php line 13 `public array $dates = [];` and line 24 `'dates' => ['required', 'array', new ResrvMinimumDuration],` (no bail). config/config.php line 36: `'minimum_reservation_period_in_days' => 1,`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [ ] **L104 — cutoff tag throws raw Exception for normal frontend conditions and returns an inconsistent schema**
  - **Where:** `src/Tags/Resrv.php:51-92`
  - **Problem:** Two distinct claims. (1) Throwing: the tag does `return throw new \Exception(...)` for missing entry id and for not-found entry (Entry::whereItemId uses firstOrFail -> ModelNotFoundException, which IS caught by catch(\Exception)). In a frontend Antlers tag this would surface as a 500. HOWEVER this is INTENTIONAL and explicitly tested: ResrvTagTest::test_cutoff_throws_exception_when_no_entry_id and test_cutoff_throws_exception_when_entry_not_found assert these exact exceptions/messages (suite passes, 15/15). So this is a deliberate design choice for a template-author error, not a bug — at most a best-practice debate about graceful degradation. (2) Inconsistent schema is REAL and not tested away: the no-schedule branch (lines 69-75) returns 5 keys, the schedule branch (lines 83-91) returns 7 (adds cutoff_datetime and is_past_cutoff). A template referencing is_past_cutoff gets null when there are no rules. (3) `return throw` is redundant (throw is already an expression-statement). Net: partially-confirmed — throwing is by-design/tested; the schema inconsistency and redundant `return` are valid low/nit cleanups.
  - **Fix:** Keep the throw behavior if intended (it is tested), but optionally consider returning a structured disabled payload for the no-id/not-found cases if graceful degradation is desired (would require updating the two assertions). Definitely emit consistent keys: add `'cutoff_datetime' => null` and `'is_past_cutoff' => null` to the no-schedule branch. Drop the redundant `return` before each `throw`.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 57 and 63: `return throw new \Exception(...)`. Entry.php line 49: `return static::query()->itemId($id)->firstOrFail();` (ModelNotFoundException extends RuntimeException extends Exception, caught at line 62). ResrvTagTest.php lines 109-127 assert the exceptions. No-schedule return lines 69-75 (5 keys) vs schedule return lines 83-91 (7 keys including cutoff_datetime/is_past_cutoff). ResrvTagTest passed: OK (15 tests, 41 assertions).
  - _best-practice · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **L105 — ResrvCheckoutRedirect::index declares array return but can fall through to null**
  - **Where:** `src/Tags/ResrvCheckoutRedirect.php:12-30`
  - **Problem:** index(): array returns only inside three branches comparing $redirectData['status'] strictly to false, true, and 'pending'. There is no final return, so any gateway whose handleRedirectBack() returns a different status value (or a malformed array missing 'status') makes the method fall off the end and implicitly return null, violating the `: array` return type and throwing a TypeError on the checkout-complete page. Built-in gateways currently return one of the three values so it works today, but downstream/custom gateways (PayPal, Mollie, etc. per UPGRADE-PAYMENT-GATEWAYS.md) are exactly the extension point that could return something else. Confirmed; low severity (latent, depends on custom gateway behavior).
  - **Fix:** Convert to a single `return match ($redirectData['status'] ?? false) { ... default => $this->makeResponse('failed', ...) };` or add an explicit final `return $this->makeResponse('failed', __('Payment failed'), __('...'));` so every path returns an array.
  - **Evidence:** Lines 21-29: three `if (...) { return $this->makeResponse(...); }` blocks for `=== false`, `=== true`, `=== 'pending'`, with nothing after line 29 before the closing brace at line 30. Method signature line 12: `public function index(): array`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

### Other

- [ ] **L107 — Stripe payment view sets `.value` on a boolean error flag**
  - **Where:** `resources/views/livewire/checkout-payment.blade.php:79-81`
  - **Problem:** In the Alpine 'payment' component errors is initialised to false (line 53). The card/validation branch correctly sets `this.errors = error.message` (line 78), but the fallback branch does `this.errors.value = "An unexpected error occurred. Please contact us.";` (line 80) — assigning a .value property onto the boolean false, which is a silent no-op (or throws in strict mode). The template binds `<span x-html="errors">` (line 38) and shows it via `x-show="errors"` (line 37), both of which still read the boolean false, so on an unexpected Stripe error the customer sees nothing. Additionally line 77 reads error.type without guarding error being undefined; stripe.confirmPayment can resolve without an error on redirect-style flows, which would itself throw. Low severity (error UX only; no charge/data impact).

  - _bug · confirmed · medium confidence_

## ⚪ Nit (49)

### Reservations & State machine

- [ ] **N1 — ReservationStatus::isTerminal() is dead code and overlaps the unrelated static terminal()**
  - **Where:** `src/Enums/ReservationStatus.php:41-61`
  - **Problem:** Two similarly-named methods encode different concepts: instance isTerminal() returns true only for EXPIRED/REFUNDED (no outbound transitions), while static terminal() returns [COMPLETED, REFUNDED, EXPIRED] (statuses excluded from active availability). The 'dead code' claim is too strong: isTerminal() has no production callers in src/, but it IS exercised by three tests (StateMachineTest.php:156-169: test_expired_is_terminal / test_refunded_is_terminal / test_pending_is_not_terminal), so it is intentional, tested API rather than dead code. terminal() is used heavily (AvailabilityRepository, ActiveReservationsGuard, RateCpController, HandlesAvailabilityQueries, AvailabilityCpController). The naming-collision maintainability concern is valid — a future maintainer could call the wrong one in an availability query (COMPLETED differs between the two) — but it is a nit.
  - **Fix:** Rename for clarity: keep the tested instance method but call it hasNoOutboundTransitions(), and rename the static set to releasesInventory()/excludedFromAvailability(). No behavioral change needed.
  - **Evidence:** ReservationStatus.php:41-47 isTerminal() => EXPIRED/REFUNDED only; 54-61 static terminal() => [COMPLETED, REFUNDED, EXPIRED]. grep: isTerminal() referenced only in StateMachineTest.php:158/163/168 (no src/ callers); terminal() referenced in AvailabilityRepository.php:330/334/373/382, ActiveReservationsGuard.php:17/34/46, RateCpController.php:143/150, HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:286/292, AvailabilityCpController.php:180.
  - _maintainability · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N2 — Vestigial getPropertyAttributeLabel() left over from the removed 'property' system**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:138-141`
  - **Problem:** getPropertyAttributeLabel() (Reservation.php:138-141) and the identical method on ChildReservation.php:45-48 just delegate to getRateLabel(). The property system was removed in favour of rates (UPGRADE_TO_RATES.md / CLAUDE.md). I confirmed neither method has any caller in src/, resources/, or tests/ — the only grep hits for 'property' are an unrelated local variable $propertyLabels in UpgradeToRates.php and a $reservation->property attribute read in RateMigrationTest.php:533 (which tests legacy-schema migration and is unrelated to this camelCase method). Keeping it only preserves the deliberately-dropped 'property' vocabulary. Nit.
  - **Fix:** Delete both getPropertyAttributeLabel() methods. If retained for a documented backward-compat template contract, add a comment referencing where it is consumed.
  - **Evidence:** Reservation.php:138-141 returns $this->getRateLabel(); ChildReservation.php:45-48 identical. grep getPropertyAttributeLabel across src/resources/tests => only the two definitions. UpgradeToRates.php hits are a local $propertyLabels variable, not this method.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N3 — array_key_exists(...) > 0 boolean-compared-as-int in validateExtraCharges**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Reservation.php:387,394`
  - **Problem:** Lines 387 and 394 use `if (array_key_exists('options', $data) > 0)` / `if (array_key_exists('extras', $data) > 0)`, comparing a bool against 0. It happens to work (true>0 true, false>0 false) but misleadingly reads as a count check. It also does not verify $data['options']/$data['extras'] is a Collection before calling ->each on the next line — unlike the parent path (validateParentExtraCharges lines 415, 421) which additionally guards with `&& $data['options']->count() > 0`. If a present-but-non-Collection value were passed, ->each would fatal. In practice the callers pass Collections, so this is a nit.
  - **Fix:** Use `if (array_key_exists('options', $data))` (or isset), and mirror the parent path's `&& $data['options']->count() > 0` guard / an instanceof Collection check for robustness.
  - **Evidence:** Reservation.php:387 `if (array_key_exists('options', $data) > 0)` then 388 `$data['options']->each(...)`. Line 394 same for extras. Parent path lines 415/421 use `array_key_exists(...) && $data[...]->count() > 0`.
  - _style · confirmed · high confidence_

### Availability & Rates

- [ ] **N4 — Per-selection dates in the cart are not bounded by the maximum reservation period**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:204-260`
  - **Problem:** It is true that validateCrossSelectionAvailability() iterates per-day over each selection's date range (line 218) and that $selections is public and not #[Locked], so a tampered client could submit a large range; ResrvMinimumDuration only runs against the live search, not the stored selections. However the practical risk is very low and heavily mitigated: the per-selection confirmAvailabilityAndPrice loop (lines 169-195) runs BEFORE validateCrossSelectionAvailability (line 197) and requires BOTH availability rows AND an exact matching price for the tampered range. A tampered far-future/huge range will not match the search-computed price (or has no availability rows), so confirmAvailabilityAndPrice returns false and throws before the per-day loop. The loop is only reachable for ranges that legitimately have availability and a matching price. Confirmed as a defensive-hardening nit, not a real vulnerability.
  - **Fix:** Optionally add an explicit guard at the top of validateMultiAvailabilityAndPrice(): for each selection assert date_start < date_end, dates in the future, and duration <= config('resrv-config.maximum_reservation_period_in_days'); reject tampered selections outright. Defense-in-depth, not required.
  - **Evidence:** Line 218: `for ($date = $start->copy(); $date->lt($end); $date->addDay())`. The price/availability gate runs first: lines 190-194 `if (! app(Availability::class)->confirmAvailabilityAndPrice($searchData, $this->entryId)) { throw ... }`; confirmAvailabilityAndPrice (Availability.php:106) returns false when status != 1 or price mismatches. Legitimate addSelections uses $this->data->dates which passed ResrvMinimumDuration during search.
  - _security · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [ ] **N5 — Redundant double base-rate resolution in cross-selection availability validation**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:212-239`
  - **Problem:** validateCrossSelectionAvailability() resolves $baseRateId via $repository->resolveBaseRateId($rateId) (line 212), keys $demandByBaseRate by that already-resolved id, then passes it to validateStandardAvailabilityForDemand($baseRateId, ...). That method immediately re-resolves with `app(AvailabilityRepository::class)->resolveBaseRateId($rateId)` (line 239). resolveBaseRateId runs Rate::withoutGlobalScopes()->find() (Repository line 39) memoized via $this->rateCache, BUT line 239 calls app(AvailabilityRepository::class) which returns a FRESH instance (the repository is not registered as a singleton in ResrvProvider), so its rateCache is empty and the find() query runs again. Confirmed: one redundant Rate::find query per base rate per checkout. Nit severity.
  - **Fix:** Drop the second resolveBaseRateId() call in validateStandardAvailabilityForDemand() since it is only ever called with an already-resolved base rate id; use the passed $rateId directly (optionally rename the param to $baseRateId). Alternatively register AvailabilityRepository as a scoped/singleton binding so rateCache is shared.
  - **Evidence:** Line 212: `$baseRateId = $repository->resolveBaseRateId($rateId);` ($repository = app(AvailabilityRepository::class), line 208). Line 226: `$this->validateStandardAvailabilityForDemand($baseRateId, $dateDemands);`. Line 239: `$resolvedRateId = app(AvailabilityRepository::class)->resolveBaseRateId($rateId);`. resolveBaseRateId (Repository 33-46) caches in $this->rateCache but the new app() instance starts empty. No singleton/scoped binding for AvailabilityRepository in ResrvProvider.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N6 — generateDatePeriods() is called with an argument it does not accept**
  - **Where:** `src/Livewire/Traits/HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:83`
  - **Problem:** Line 83 calls `$this->generateDatePeriods($this->data)` but the method is declared with no parameters (line 312: `protected function generateDatePeriods(): Collection`) and reads $this->data internally. PHP silently ignores the extra positional argument, so it works, but the call site is misleading. Harmless maintainability nit, confirmed.
  - **Fix:** Remove the argument: `$this->generateDatePeriods()`.
  - **Evidence:** Line 83: `return $this->generateDatePeriods($this->data)->map(...)`. Line 312: `protected function generateDatePeriods(): Collection {` with body reading `$this->data->dates['date_start']` (line 314), no parameters declared.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N7 — confirmAvailabilityAndPrice compares money with loose != on formatted strings**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Availability.php:106`
  - **Problem:** Line 106 compares $availability['data']['price'] != $data['price'] with a loose !=. Verified that in all current call sites both operands are Price::format() decimal strings: the left comes from getSpecificItemCollection -> getResultForItem (Availability.php:506 'price' => ...->format()) and the right is supplied as data_get($this->availability,'data.price') (HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:142) or an ->format()/per-unit-string price (HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:176-187), or $data['price'] passed through Reservation::checkAvailability (Reservation.php:336). Price::format() uses moneyphp's DecimalMoneyFormatter so both sides are like '100.00' and match. So there is no active bug — this is a latent fragility, not the medium/correctness issue implied. If a future call site passes a non-formatted value (int 100, or '100' vs '100.00'), the loose != would falsely report drift. Severity is a nit/maintainability note, consistent with the reviewer's own low confidence.
  - **Fix:** Defensive, not urgent: compare via the money layer, e.g. Price::create((string) $availability['data']['price'])->equals(Price::create((string) $data['price'])), so the check is decimal-safe and format-insensitive regardless of how callers produce the price string. No behavior change for current callers.
  - **Evidence:** Availability.php:106 if ($availability['message']['status'] != 1 || $availability['data']['price'] != $data['price']). Left operand produced by ->format() at Availability.php:506/538; right operand at HandlesAvailabilityQueries.php:142 data_get(...,'data.price') and 176-187 (->format() or per-unit string). Price::format() (Money/Price.php:99-105) returns a DecimalMoneyFormatter string. Price::equals (line 84-87) is the money-safe comparison the codebase otherwise mandates.
  - _best-practice · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N8 — block()/unblock() guards prevent recovery when blocked stock was partially consumed**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Availability.php:222-248`
  - **Problem:** The fragility analysis is partly valid but the practical risk is essentially nil: grep confirms block()/unblock() have NO first-party callers anywhere in src/ — only the `available_blocked` property is referenced (in $fillable line 38 and inside the two methods themselves). The methods are saveQuietly() writes with no transaction/lock (lines 228, 242). The reviewer's concern about a double-block overwriting available_blocked is real in principle: a second block() when available is already 0 returns false WITHOUT updating available_blocked (lines 224-233), which is actually the safe behavior (it preserves the original); the genuinely fragile case would be if available were mutated between block and unblock, but with no callers this cannot happen. Given zero callers, this is dead/unused API with a fragile-but-currently-inert invariant. Severity nit, not low.
  - **Fix:** If these methods are kept, wrap block()/unblock() in a DB transaction with lockForUpdate and make block() idempotent (no-op when available_blocked !== null) so the stored original is never overwritten. Otherwise consider removing the unused methods. No urgency given no callers exist.
  - **Evidence:** grep across src/ shows block( defined only at Availability.php:222 and unblock at 236, with no `->block(`/`->unblock(` call sites. available_blocked appears only at line 38 ($fillable), 226, 239, 240, 241. block() lines 224-233 and unblock() 239-245 use `$this->saveQuietly()` with no transaction or lockForUpdate.
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N9 — scopeForEntry never caches a null (missing-collection) lookup**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Rate.php:133-134`
  - **Problem:** Accurate. `static::$entryCollectionCache[$entryId] ??= Entry::where('item_id', $entryId)->value('collection');` does not memoize negatives: `??=` is `$a = $a ?? b`, and when value('collection') returns null (no resrv_entries row for that id), the cache holds null, so every subsequent forEntry() call within the request re-runs the `value('collection')` query for that not-found id. Only a latent micro-inefficiency for non-existent/stale entry ids, hence nit, but it does contradict the static cache's intent for the not-found case.
  - **Fix:** Memoize negatives with array_key_exists: `if (! array_key_exists($entryId, static::$entryCollectionCache)) { static::$entryCollectionCache[$entryId] = Entry::where('item_id', $entryId)->value('collection'); } $collection = static::$entryCollectionCache[$entryId];`.
  - **Evidence:** Rate.php:133-134 `$collection = static::$entryCollectionCache[$entryId] ??= Entry::where('item_id', $entryId)->value('collection');`. PHP `$x ??= y` re-evaluates y whenever $x is null, so a cached null re-triggers the query.
  - _performance · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N10 — group_concat/string_agg used for price summation has no defined row ordering and skips NULLs**
  - **Where:** `src/Repositories/AvailabilityRepository.php:23-31`
  - **Problem:** Both observations are technically true but currently dormant, so severity is a nit not low. (1) groupConcat() (lines 23-31) emits `group_concat(price)` / `string_agg(price::text, ',')` with no ORDER BY, so concatenation order is engine-dependent. For the actual consumers this is harmless: createPricesCollection() (Availability.php:573) explodes and SUMs the values via Price::add — order-independent. The reviewer's own caveat ('not guaranteed index-aligned IF any caller ever zips them') is hypothetical; I found no caller that positionally zips `prices` against `dates`. (2) Both aggregates drop NULLs, but the price column is NOT NULL (float(8,2) per the migration/factory defaults), so a NULL price row cannot currently occur. Both are latent robustness concerns only.
  - **Fix:** Optional hardening only: wrap with COALESCE(price,0) inside the aggregate to be NULL-safe, and add a deterministic ORDER BY (e.g. by date) if any future caller consumes prices/dates positionally. Not required for current behavior.
  - **Evidence:** groupConcat (lines 27-30) `'pgsql' => "string_agg({$column}::text, ',')", default => "group_concat({$column})"` — no ORDER BY, both drop NULLs. Consumer createPricesCollection (Availability.php:573) `collect(explode(',', $prices))->transform(fn ($price) => Price::create($price))` then summed via `$start->add(...$pricesCollection->toArray())` (HandlesPricing.php:62) — a pure sum, order-independent. No positional zip of prices vs dates found in callers.
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

- [ ] **N11 — HandlesOrdering::changeOrder reorders the entire table with no scoping**
  - **Where:** `src/Traits/HandlesOrdering.php:7-27`
  - **Problem:** The factual observations are correct: HandlesOrdering::changeOrder() does `$this->orderBy('order')->get()` with no WHERE clause (line 13) and uses loose `==` (lines 9, 18), so it renumbers every row of the model's table; and Rate does NOT use this trait — it has its own scoped strict-comparison changeOrder() (Rate.php:156-181). The two implementations have genuinely diverged. However this is not a bug in the rates unit: Rate is correct, and the unscoped trait is only applied to Extra/OptionValue/etc., where each model's table is intended to be globally ordered (no collection partitioning), so 'reorders the entire table' is arguably the intended behavior there, not a defect. The only actionable risk is the refactoring hazard the finding itself names. Downgraded from low to nit — it is a documentation/divergence note, not a defect.
  - **Fix:** Optional: add a class-doc note on HandlesOrdering that it is intentionally global and must not be applied to Rate (which is collection/base-scoped); or tighten `==` to `===`. No functional change required for the rates unit.
  - **Evidence:** HandlesOrdering.php:13 `$items = $this->orderBy('order')->get()->keyBy('id');` (no scoping); :9 `if ($this->order == $order)`; :18 `if ($count == $order)`. Rate.php:156-181 uses `(int) $this->order === $order` and `static::where('collection', …)->where('base_rate_id', …)`.
  - _maintainability · partially-confirmed · medium confidence_

### Lifecycle (events / listeners / jobs)

- [ ] **N12 — Redundant Carbon::parse on an already-cast datetime attribute**

Harmless; purely a readability nit. Note: prefer ->copy() to avoid mutating the model's created_at in place.

- [ ] **N13 — Inconsistent expiry boundary: job uses strict `<`, getReservation uses `<=`**
  - **Where:** `src/Jobs/ExpireReservations.php:35-36`
  - **Problem:** ExpireReservations expires when `$expireAt < Carbon::now()` (strict, line 36), whereas the read-path expiry in getReservation() uses `$expireAt <= Carbon::now()` (HandlesReservationQueries.php:60). A reservation sitting at the exact boundary instant is treated as expired by the read path but not by the background sweep. Purely cosmetic (sub-second window) but the two implementations of the same rule should agree.
  - **Fix:** Use the same operator in both places (prefer `<=`): `if ($expireAt <= Carbon::now())` in ExpireReservations.
  - **Evidence:** ExpireReservations.php:36 `if ($expireAt < Carbon::now())`. HandlesReservationQueries.php:60 `if ($expireAt <= Carbon::now())`.
  - _correctness · confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N14 — AddAffiliateToReservation attaches the affiliate without a duplicate guard, unlike AssociateAffiliateFromCoupon**
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/AddAffiliateToReservation.php:11-13`
  - **Problem:** AddAffiliateToReservation unconditionally calls `$event->reservation->affiliate()->attach(...)` on ReservationCreated with no existence guard, whereas AssociateAffiliateFromCoupon guards before attaching (per the finding; the affiliate() pivot resrv_reservation_affiliate has no enforced uniqueness). Currently safe because ReservationCreated fires exactly once per reservation, so no duplicate row is produced today. The concern is purely defensive/idempotency hygiene — if ReservationCreated were ever re-dispatched, a duplicate pivot row could appear. Low/nit; not an active bug.
  - **Fix:** Make the attach idempotent: `$event->reservation->affiliate()->syncWithoutDetaching([$event->data->affiliate->id => ['fee' => $event->data->affiliate->fee]]);` or add an exists() guard mirroring AssociateAffiliateFromCoupon.

ReservationCreated is dispatched once per createReservation/createMultiReservation.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · medium confidence_

- [ ] **N15 — IncreaseAvailability handler and incrementMultiple lack the event type-hint used by DecreaseAvailability**
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/IncreaseAvailability.php:11-40`
  - **Problem:** handle($event) and incrementMultiple($event) are untyped, while the symmetric DecreaseAvailability uses `handle(ReservationCreated $event)`. IncreaseAvailability is wired to three events (ReservationExpired, ReservationCancelled, ReservationRefunded) that each independently expose a public $reservation property but share no common interface. A shared interface or union type-hint would document the contract and let static analysis catch misuse. Cosmetic.
  - **Fix:** Introduce a small interface (e.g. HasReservation exposing the reservation) implemented by ReservationExpired/Cancelled/Refunded, or use a union type `ReservationExpired|ReservationCancelled|ReservationRefunded`, and type-hint the listener parameters.

DecreaseAvailability.php:12 `public function handle(ReservationCreated $event): void`. $listen maps ReservationExpired/Cancelled/Refunded -> IncreaseAvailability; all three events declare `public $reservation;`.

- [ ] **N16 — cascadeOnDelete on resrv_entry_extra never fires because the parent is soft-deleted**
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase.php:12`
  - **Problem:** resrv_entry_extra.entry_id is declared ->constrained('resrv_entries')->cascadeOnDelete() (2024_11_22_000000_create_entry_extra_table.php:13). Because the Entry model uses SoftDeletes, the EntryDeleted listener's ->delete() issues an UPDATE (set deleted_at), never a SQL DELETE, so the DB-level FK cascade never triggers - pivot rows stay attached to the soft-deleted mirror. This is effectively the intended/benign behavior (the pivot survives so a restored entry keeps its extras), but the migration's cascadeOnDelete is misleading: it implies pivot cleanup on entry deletion that never happens (only a forceDelete would trigger it). Documentation/maintainability nit, no functional bug.
  - **Fix:** Either drop the misleading cascadeOnDelete (it can never trigger under the soft-delete model) or add a code/migration comment that the pivot is only cleaned on forceDelete, so future maintainers don't rely on a cascade that does not run.
  - **Evidence:** `$table->foreignId('entry_id')->constrained('resrv_entries')->cascadeOnDelete();` (migration line 13). Parent delete is soft: SoftDeleteResrvEntryFromDatabase.php:12 + Entry uses SoftDeletes. A soft delete is an UPDATE, so the FK ON DELETE CASCADE is never invoked.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

### Pricing & Money

- [ ] **N17 — AddDynamicPricingsToReservation pivot `order` uses the post-sort collection key, not a sequential rank**
  - **Where:** `src/Listeners/AddDynamicPricingsToReservation.php:22-24`
  - **Problem:** The mechanism is real but the finding's impact justification is partly wrong. getToApply() returns DynamicPricing::$toApply. For the non-parent path $toApply is checkAllParameters()'s return, which ends in `$dynamicPricingThatApplies->sortBy('order')` (DynamicPricing.php:391); sortBy() preserves the ORIGINAL push-order integer keys, so `each(function ($pricing, $key) ...)` writes those original keys as the pivot order rather than a 0-based sorted rank. For the parent path $toApply is built with `->values()` (Availability.php:623), making keys 0-based — so the two paths are inconsistent, as claimed. HOWEVER the finding states the pivot order 'is never read back'; that is inaccurate. UpdateCouponAppliedToReservation.php:28-30 reads `resrv_reservation_dynamic_pricing.order` via ->max() to place a newly-applied coupon last. The impact is still negligible because 'max + 1' puts the coupon after the highest existing order regardless of whether the existing values are original keys or true ranks; ReservationCpController.php:176 reads $pricing->order which is the DynamicPricing model column (relation is withPivot('data') only), not the pivot, so it is unaffected. Net: a misleading-but-harmless stored value plus a parent/non-parent inconsistency.
  - **Fix:** Call `->values()` before `each()` (or use an incrementing counter) so the pivot order is a true 0-based rank consistent with the parent path: `$dynamicPricingData->getToApply()->values()->each(fn ($pricing, $key) => ...)`.
  - **Evidence:** checkAllParameters returns `$dynamicPricingThatApplies->sortBy('order')` (DynamicPricing.php:391) — keys preserved. Listener: `->each(function ($pricing, $key) ... attach($pricing->id, ['data' => ..., 'order' => $key])`. Parent path: `$dynamicPricing->toApply = $allPricings->unique('id')->values();` (Availability.php:623). Pivot order IS read at UpdateCouponAppliedToReservation.php:29-30 `->select('resrv_reservation_dynamic_pricing.order')->max(...)`.
  - _correctness · partially-confirmed · high confidence_

- [ ] **N18 — Dead method DynamicPricing::getAmount()**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/DynamicPricing.php:59-66`
  - **Problem:** DynamicPricing::getAmount($value) (lines 59-66) has no callers in src/, resources/, or tests/ — the only grep hits for 'getAmount' are this definition and the unrelated Price::getAmount() at Price.php:123. It also returns inconsistent types (raw $value for percent, a Price for fixed). Harmless dead code.
  - **Fix:** Remove the method; if it is intended public API, document and unify the return type.
  - **Evidence:** grep 'getAmount' across src/ resources/ tests/ returns only DynamicPricing.php:59 (definition) and Price.php:123 ($this->money->getAmount(), unrelated). No invocation of the model method anywhere.
  - _maintainability · confirmed · high confidence_

### Extras / Options / Cutoff

- [ ] **N19 — ResrvCutoff::process reads $data['enable_cutoff'] without null-coalesce on the return line**
  - **Where:** `src/Fieldtypes/ResrvCutoff.php:75`
  - **Problem:** Line 66 reads the flag safely as ($data['enable_cutoff'] ?? false), but the return at line 75 uses the bare $data['enable_cutoff']. If the submitted data omits that key, line 75 raises an undefined-array-key warning which is caught by the surrounding try/catch and returns the raw $data, masking the inconsistency. The two reads of the same flag should match. Low real-world impact since the UI always submits the key.
  - **Fix:** return ($data['enable_cutoff'] ?? false) ? $data : null; to match line 66.
  - **Evidence:** ResrvCutoff.php:66 if ($data['enable_cutoff'] ?? false) vs :75 return $data['enable_cutoff'] ? $data : null; both inside the try/catch (:62-78) that returns $data on any exception.

- [ ] **N20 — Dead/unsafe priceForReservation() assumes a non-null quantity**

It reads $reservation->quantity directly, which is null for parent reservations (quantity lives on children), so if ever wired up it would misprice parents. Dead code with a latent correctness trap.

- [ ] **N21 — scopeEntriesWithConditions selects both tables' '*', colliding timestamp columns**
  - **Where:** `src/Models/Extra.php:231`
  - **Problem:** ->select('resrv_extras.*', 'resrv_extra_conditions.*') returns overlapping created_at/updated_at from both tables; the second silently overwrites the first. Note resrv_extra_conditions PK is extra_id (ExtraCondition.php:23), so it has no id column and resrv_extras.id is not clobbered; the consumer requiredExtrasForEntry only reads id and conditions, so it is harmless today. Selecting overlapping wildcards is fragile and will surprise any future field added to either table.
  - **Fix:** Select only needed columns explicitly, e.g. ->select('resrv_extras.id', 'resrv_extra_conditions.conditions').
